الأبدان بينهما فيقال للذي له قرابتان ثلاثة أسهم سهمان لأن أباه ذكر، وسهم لأن أباه أنثى، وللتي لها قرابة واحدة سهم واحد لأن أباها أنثى فحصل للذي له قرابتان ثلاثة أسهم فما وصل إلى ذي القرابتين من
Chapter on clarifying the inheritance of one who has two relations from the children of daughters. Know that when in a single person two relations from children of daughters come together, and its picture is: a man has two daughters; one daughter has a daughter, and the other has a son. Then the son married the daughter of the daughter, and between them was born a daughter. Then the man who had two daughters died and left this girl. So she is the daughter of the man's daughter and also the son's daughter of the man, and she had two relations, and he has a daughter of the daughter of another daughter with one relation. And Shaykh al-Islam mentioned in his commentary that according to the opinion of Abu Yusuf, the division is by bodies not by fathers, and their bodies are equal, so the wealth is between them half and half. According to Muhammad, division is by fathers and he inherits from two directions considering fathers. So it is said that the one with one relation has one share because her father is female; the one with two relations has one share because her father is female and two shares because her father is male. So the wealth is between them into four: two shares go to her without contest – what reached her from the direction of her male father, she takes alone; and the share that reached her from the direction of her female father is added to what is in the hand of the one with one relation, due to the agreement of both their fathers in femininity, so it becomes two shares considering their bodies. Then if he leaves a son of a daughter of a daughter, and she is a daughter of a son of his son, and he also leaves a son of a daughter of a daughter; according to Abu Yusuf, division is by bodies, one is male and the other female, and they are equal in degree, so the wealth is between them with the male taking twice the share of the female based on three. According to Muhammad, the wealth is divided by fathers then by bodies. So it is said: the one with one relation, she is the daughter of his daughter, has one share because her father is female; the one with two relations, she has three shares, two shares go to her without contest – what reached her from the direction of her male father and what reached her from the direction of her female father, and that share does not go to her alone but is added to what is in the hand of the one with one relation, which is one share, and is divided between them with the male taking twice the female share based on three, due to the agreement of their relations in these two shares and the difference of their bodies. And dividing two shares into three does not come straight and there is no agreement between them in anything. So multiply the original estate, which is four, by three, making twelve shares, this entire wealth, and from it the case emerges. Then the one with two relations had two shares without contest, we multiplied them by three, so she gets six. And what did not come straight between them with contest, two shares, we multiplied them by three, so they become six, divided between them with the male taking twice the female share considering bodies; the one with two relations gives two shares because she is female, and four shares to the one with one relation because he is male. So the one with two relations gets eight, six without contest. This is what we mentioned if the one with two relations is female and the one with one relation is female. According to Abu Yusuf, the wealth is in thirds considering bodies between them; for the one with two relations two shares because it is male, and for the one with one relation because it is female. And according to Muhammad, division by fathers then by bodies: it is said that the one with two relations has three shares, two shares because his father is male, one share because his father is female; and the one with one relation has one share because her father is female. So the one with two relations got three shares. So what reached the one with two relations from...
Source pages p. 403

Commentary
This is a detailed intellectual exercise in faraid, dealing with a rare scenario where a person inherits from two directions simultaneously (dual kinship). The case involves a man with two daughters; one daughter has a daughter, the other a son. The son marries the daughter of the daughter and has a daughter (call her X). So X is the daughter of the man's granddaughter through his daughter's son, and also the daughter of the man's other granddaughter through his daughter's daughter? Actually, the family tree is complex: the man (M) has two daughters: D1 and D2. D1 has a daughter (G1), D2 has a son (G2). G2 marries G1 and they have a daughter (X). Then M dies leaving X and another relative? The text says 'he left this' (i.e., X) and also 'he has a daughter of the daughter of another daughter with one relation' (another granddaughter from a different daughter? Possibly G1 from another wife? The OCR is corrupted). The key is that X has two relations: she is both a granddaughter through her mother (from M's daughter D1) and a granddaughter through her father (from M's daughter D2 via G2). So she has dual kinship (both maternal and paternal lines through M's daughters). Another child (Y) has only one relation (e.g., a granddaughter through a single line). The dispute is how to divide between X and Y. Abu Yusuf: consider only the individuals (bodies) – they are both female? Actually, in one version, both are female, so they get half each. Muhammad: first assign shares based on the ancestors (fathers) of each: X's father is male (son of M's daughter) so gives her two shares from that side? And her mother (female) gives one share. Y's father is female (daughter of M's daughter) so one share. Total shares 4, but then some shares are contested. The calculation becomes more complex in the second example with a male and female. The text works through a detailed arithmetic with a base of 12 shares. The conclusion: under Muhammad, the one with dual kinship ends up with 8 out of 12, while under Abu Yusuf, if both female, it's half; if one male and one female, it's double the male's share. This case illustrates the methodological difference between prioritizing individual bodies (Abu Yusuf) versus ancestral lineage (Muhammad) in faraid. The ultimate distribution depends on which principle is followed.

Key Terms
ذو قرابتين (dhu qarabatayn): A person who has two kinship lines to the deceased, e.g., through both a son and a daughter of the deceased.
القسمة على الأبدان (al-qismatu 'ala al-abdan): Division of inheritance based on counting each heir as a single individual, irrespective of lineage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the dual kinship case, what is the main difference between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad's method?
A) Abu Yusuf considers lineages, Muhammad considers bodies.
B) Abu Yusuf divides by bodies, Muhammad first assigns shares by fathers then divides by bodies.
C) Both agree on half each.
D) Muhammad gives all to the dual kinship heir.

Key Takeaway
Dual kinship requires a layered calculation: Abu Yusuf's simple body count and Muhammad's lineage-based method yield different shares, illustrating the depth of Hanafi faraid reasoning.

Faraid — Inheritance

Inheritance of a Granddaughter with Dual Relationship
Introduces and rules on a case where a granddaughter inherits from two paths.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to compare the methods of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad for dividing inheritance when an heir has dual relationships, and calculate the shares under each method.

Core Idea
When an heir inherits through two paths, Abu Yusuf divides by persons; Muhammad divides by ancestors first, then pools conflicting shares.

This passage presents a classical intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding the inheritance of a granddaughter who is related through both a son and a daughter. The case illustrates two fundamentally different approaches to dividing the estate when an heir has multiple kinship ties. Understanding this dispute reveals how the school's internal methodological differences affect actual share distribution.

Guided Path
1
Map the family tree
Identify the deceased, the two granddaughters, and how one has dual relationships (through both a son and a daughter).
The dual-relation granddaughter is the child of an intermarriage between the deceased's grandson and granddaughter.
2
Apply Abu Yusuf's rule
Divide simply by number of persons (heads), ignoring multiple relationships. Both granddaughters are female, so each gets half.
Abu Yusuf's rule is 'al-qismah 'ala al-abdan'.
3
Apply Muhammad's rule
First assign shares based on ancestors (آباء), then pool conflicting shares and redivide by persons. The dual-relation gets 3 shares initially (2 from male ancestor, 1 from female), but the female-ancestor share is contested.
Muhammad's rule is 'al-qismah 'ala al-aba' then 'ala al-abdan'.
4
Compare outcomes
Under Abu Yusuf, dual-relation gets 1/2; under Muhammad, she gets 3/4. The thamarah al-khilaf is a significant difference in share.
This shows the practical consequence of the ikhtilaf.
5
Extend to mixed-gender scenario
Apply both methods to the second case with a male and a female heir. Under Abu Yusuf, male takes double female share; under Muhammad, the dual-relation female gets 8/12, single-relation male gets 4/12.
The principles remain consistent.
6
Identify the mufta bihi
Later authorities (faradiyyun of Transoxiana, al-Qadi al-Imam) preferred Abu Yusuf's view, so it is the operative position.
This does not invalidate Muhammad's view; it is a legitimate ikhtilaf with a chosen tarjih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصورة هذا أن يكون لرجل ابنتان لإحدى ابنتيه ابنة وللأخرى ابن من فتزوج الابن الابنة بنت الابنة فحدث بينهما ابنة ثم مات الرجل الذي له ابنتان وترك هذه فهذه ابنة ابنة الرجل وهي أيضاً ابنة ابن الرجل وكان لها قرابتان وله ابنة ابنة بنت أخرى لها قرابة واحدة، وذكر شيخ الإسلام في شرحه أن على قول أبي يوسف القسمة على الأبدان لا على الآباء وبدنهما متفق فيكون المال بينهما نصفين وعند محمد يقسم على الآباء ويورث من جهتين باعتبار الآباء فيقال بأن التي لها قرابة واحدة لها سهم لأن أباها أنثى والتي لها قرابتان سهم من رجل لأن أباها أنثى وسهمان لأن أباها ذكر فصار المال بينهما على أربعة : سهمان يسلم لها بلا منازعة وهو مات وصل إليها من جهة أبيها الذكر تنفرد به، والسهم الذي وصل إليها من جهة أبيها الأنثى يضم إلى ما في يد التي لها قرابة واحدة لاتفاق أبيهما في الأنوثة فيصير سهمان باعتبار ،بدنهما، فإن ترك ابنه ابنة بنت وهي ابنة ابن ابنه وترك أيضاً ابن ابنة ابنة؛ أما عند أبي يوسف فالقسمة على الأبدان وأحدهما ذكر والأخرى أنثى وقد استويا في الدرجة فيكون المال بينهما للذكر مثل حظ الأنثيين على ثلاثة وأما عند محمد يقسم المال على الأباء ثم على الأبدان فيقال للذي له قرابة واحدة وهي بنت ابنته سهم لأن أباه أنثى وللذي له قرابتان فهي ثلاثة أسهم يسلم لها سهمان بلا منازعة وهو ما وصل إليها من جهة أبيها الذكر وما وصل إليها من جهة أبيها الأنثى وذلك سهم لا يسلم لها بل يضم إلى ما في يد الذي لها قرابة واحدة وهو سهم فيقسم بينهما للذكر مثل حظ الأنثيين على ثلاثة لاتفاق قرابتهما في هذين السهمين واختلاف أبدانهما وقسمة سهمين على ثلاثة لا يستقيم ولا موافقة بينهما في شيء فاضرب أصل الفريضة وذلك أربعة في ثلاثة فصار اثني عشرة سهماً هذا المال ، جميع ومنه تخرج المسألة فإن التي لها قرابتان كان لها سهمان بلا منازعة ضربناهما في ثلاثة فصار له ستة، والذي لم يكن يستقيم بينهما مع المنازعة سهمان ضربناهما في ثلاثة فصار ستة بينها للذكر مثل حظ الأنثيين باعتبار الأبدان التي لها قرابتان ثلثها وذلك سهمان لأنها أنثى وأربعة للذي لها قرابة واحدة لأنه ذكر فحصل للذي لها قرابتان ثمانية ستة بلا منازعة.
The form of this is that a man has two daughters; one daughter has a daughter, and the other has a son. Then the son married the daughter of the daughter, and a daughter was born to them. Then the man who had two daughters died and left this (granddaughter). So she is the daughter of the man's daughter, and she is also the daughter of the man's son, so she has two relationships. And he left another granddaughter (daughter of his daughter's daughter) who has one relationship. Shaykh al-Islam mentioned in his commentary that according to Abu Yusuf, division is by persons, not by ancestors, and their persons are the same (both female), so the wealth is divided between them in halves. According to Muhammad, division is by ancestors, and inheritance comes from two sides considering ancestors. So it is said that the one with one relationship has one share because her father is female, and the one with two relationships has one share from a man because her father is female, and two shares because her father is male. So the wealth between them becomes four shares: two shares are secured for her without dispute, which came to her from the side of her male father, she takes them exclusively; and the share that came to her from the side of her female father is added to what is in the hand of the one with one relationship due to the agreement of their fathers in femininity, so they become two shares considering their persons. There is another case: if he leaves his son's daughter's daughter, who is his son's son's daughter, and also leaves his daughter's son's son; according to Abu Yusuf, division is by persons: one is male and the other female, and they are equal in degree, so the wealth is divided between them as male gets double female share, making three shares. According to Muhammad, wealth is divided by ancestors then by persons. So it is said that the one with one relationship, who is the daughter of his daughter, has one share because her father is female. The one with two relationships has three shares: two are secured without dispute, which came from the side of her male father; and the share from her female father is not secured but is added to the share of the one with one relationship, making a total of two shares to be divided between them as male gets double female share, due to agreement of their relationship in these two shares and difference of their persons. Dividing two shares by three does not work evenly, and there is no concordance between them in anything. So multiply the base of the estate, which is four, by three, giving twelve shares. This is all the wealth, and from it the case is resolved. The one with two relationships had two shares without dispute; we multiply them by three, giving six. The two shares that were not divisible between them with dispute are multiplied by three, giving six to be divided between them as male gets double female share by considering persons: the one with two relationships gets one third of that, which is two shares because she is female, and the one with one relationship gets four because he is male. So the one with two relationships gets eight: six without dispute.
Source pages p. 403

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani regarding the inheritance of a granddaughter who has dual relationships (ذو قرابتين) because she is simultaneously the daughter of the man's son and the daughter of his daughter. The case arises from a specific family tree: a man has two daughters; one daughter has a daughter, the other has a son; the son marries the daughter of the first daughter, and they have a daughter. When the original man dies, he leaves two granddaughters: one is the child of the intermarriage (dual relation) and the other is a simple granddaughter from the other daughter (single relation). The key difference between the two imams is that Abu Yusuf divides the estate based on the number of persons (أبدان) regardless of the number of inheritance paths, whereas Muhammad divides based on the ancestors (آباء) first, considering each path as a separate source of shares. In this first scenario, both granddaughters are female, so under Abu Yusuf they split equally. Under Muhammad, the dual-relation granddaughter gets three shares (two from the male ancestor and one from the female ancestor) out of a base of four, but one of those shares is contested because it comes from the female ancestor and must be pooled with the single-relation granddaughter's share, then re-divided between them as persons. The passage also introduces a second scenario with mixed genders (male and female) to illustrate the application of the rules. The commentary by 'Shaykh al-Islam' (likely Zayn al-Din al-Zayla'i) is referenced. The author then explains the calculation when the numbers do not divide evenly, requiring multiplication to find a common denominator. The final result gives the dual-relation heir eight out of twelve shares.

Key Terms
ذو قرابتين (dhu qarabatayn): An heir who has two kinship ties to the deceased, e.g., through both a son and a daughter.
القسمة على الأبدان (al-qismah 'ala al-abdan): Abu Yusuf's method: distribute the estate based on the number of persons (heads), regardless of multiple relationships.
القسمة على الآباء (al-qismah 'ala al-aba'): Muhammad's method: first assign shares based on the ancestors through whom inheritance flows.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Division by number of persons (أبدان)
C) Division by number of relationships
D) Division by gender only

Key Takeaway
When an heir has dual relationships, Abu Yusuf divides by persons, while Muhammad divides by ancestors first; the relied-upon view is Abu Yusuf's.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Dual-Relation Inheritance with Two Female Heirs
Intra-Hanafi dispute on dual-relation inheritance with two female heirs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate inheritance shares for two female heirs where one has dual relationships, using both Abu Yusuf's and Muhammad's methods, and explain the resulting difference.

Core Idea
Abu Yusuf divides by persons; Muhammad divides by ancestors first, then persons — leading to different shares for dual-relation heirs.

In this lesson, we continue our exploration of dual-relationship inheritance, now focusing on a scenario where both heirs are female. This case reveals a subtle intra-Hanafi disagreement between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani. Their differing approaches to first dividing by persons versus first dividing by ancestors yield different final shares. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply faraid principles to non-standard heir configurations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the heirs
Two female heirs: one with dual relationships (e.g., daughter of a son and daughter of a daughter), one with a single relationship.
2
Apply Abu Yusuf's method (al-badan)
He divides the estate into three shares: two for the dual-relation heir (because she inherits from two sides, analogous to a male) and one for the single-relation heir.
Persons-based division: dual gets 2/3, single gets 1/3.
3
Apply Muhammad's method (al-aba' then al-badan)
First assign shares by ancestors: dual gets 3 shares (2 from male ancestor, 1 from female ancestor), single gets 1 share. Then pool the share from the female ancestor (1) with the single's share, and divide that pool as if dual is male and single is female (2:1).
Pool = 2 shares, but division by 3 requires multiplying the base (4) by 3 to get 12.
4
Calculate final distribution
After multiplication to 12: dual initially 9, single 3. Dual gives 3 (from female ancestor) to pool, single gives all 3. Pool=6. Dual gets 4 (2/3 of 6), single gets 2. Dual final=6+4=10, single final=2. So dual gets 10/12 = 5/6, single 2/12 = 1/6.
Under Abu Yusuf: dual 8/12, single 4/12. Under Muhammad: dual 10/12, single 2/12.
5
Compare the practical difference
Muhammad's method gives the dual-relation heir a larger share (5/6 vs 2/3) because her ancestral connections are fully accounted before pooling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هذا الذي ذكرنا إذا كانت التي لها قرابتان أنثى والتي لها قرابة واحدة أنثى أما عند أبي يوسف فالمال أثلاثاً باعتبار الأبدان بينهما فللتي لها قرابتان سهمان لأنه ذكر وللتي لها قرابة واحدة لأنها أنثى. وأما عند محمد القسمة باعتبار الآباء ثم باعتبار الأبدان بينهما فيقال للذي له قرابتان ثلاثة أسهم سهمان لأن أباه ذكر، وسهم لأن أباه أنثى، وللتي لها قرابة واحدة سهم واحد لأن أباها أنثى فحصل للذي له قرابتان ثلاثة أسهم فما وصل إلى ذي القرابتين من جهة أبيه الأنثى وذلك سهم يضم إلى ما في يد الآخر وفي يدها سهم فيكون بينهما باعتبار الأبدان على ثلاثة للذكر مثل حظ الأنثيين لاتفاق آبائهما واختلاف أبنائهما، وقسمة سهمين على ثلاثة لا يستقيم ولا توافق بينهما فتضرب أصل الفريضة وذلك أربعة في ثلاثة فيصير اثني عشر هذا جميع المال، ومنه تخرج المسألة. فإن ترك ابنة ابنة وهي ابنة ابن ابنة وترك أيضاً ابنة ابنة ابنة وترك أيضاً ابنة ابن ابنة أخرى فعلى قول أبي يوسف يقسم بينهم باعتبار الأبدان على ثلاثة أسهم لأن أبدانهم متفقة فإن كلهن أناث، وأما عند محمد القسمة على الآباء ثم على الأبدان فيقال لابنة ابنة البنت التي لها قرابة واحدة سهم لأن أباها أنثى ولابنة ابن البنت التي لها قرابة واحدة سهمان لأن أباها ذكر ولمن لها قرابتان لها ثلاثة أسهم من جهتين سهم من جهة إن أباها أنثى وسهمان من جهة إن أباها ذكر فيكون المال بينهم على ستة باعتبار الآباء ثم الأبدان متفق تجيء قسمة أخرى باعتبار الأبدان؛ هذه الجملة على هذا الترتيب أوردها شيخ الإسلام في شرحه. وذكر القاضي الإمام قول محمد رحمه الله على نحو ما ذكر شيخ الإسلام.
This is what we mentioned when the one with two relationships is female and the one with one relationship is female. As for according to Abu Yusuf, the wealth is in thirds considering the persons between them: for the one with two relationships, two shares because she is male? Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of dual-relationship inheritance by presenting two further scenarios. The first scenario (lines 1-9 of the Arabic) is the case where both heirs are female (the dual-relation and the single-relation are both female). Under Abu Yusuf, since they are both female, he treats the dual-relation heir as having the share of a male? The Arabic says 'لأنه ذكر' which is odd because 'هو' is masculine. Possibly a corruption; the intended meaning is that the dual-relation heir is given a double share because she inherits from two sides, analogized to a male. Under Muhammad, the dual-relation heir gets 3 shares out of 4 initially, but the share from the female ancestor is pooled with the single-relation heir's share, leading to a base of 12 after multiplication. The second scenario involves three female heirs: one with one relationship from a female line, one with one relationship from a male line, and one with dual relationships. Under Abu Yusuf, since all are female, division is equal into thirds. Under Muhammad, they first get shares by ancestors: 1, 2, and 3 respectively (total 6), then since all are female, the pooled shares (?) are divided equally? The text says 'ثم الأبدان متفق تجيء قسمة أخرى باعتبار الأبدان' meaning since their persons are the same (all female), they then divide the estate equally? But the earlier step already gave them shares. Possibly the meaning is that after ancestor-based shares, the portions that are contested (like from the female ancestor) are pooled and re-divided equally because they are all female. The author concludes that this summary is from Shaykh al-Islam (likely al-Zayla'i), and al-Qadi al-Imam agrees with Muhammad's method as reported by Shaykh al-Islam.

Key Terms
أصل الفريضة (asl al-faridah): The base number used to calculate shares in inheritance problems, adjusted to avoid fractions.
باعتبار الأبدان (bi'tibar al-abdan): Considering the persons; dividing based on the number of individuals and their gender.
باعتبار الآباء (bi'tibar al-aba'): Considering the ancestors; dividing based on the ancestral connections (male/female ancestors).

For two female heirs, Abu Yusuf gives the dual-relation 2/3, Muhammad gives 5/6 — the method of initial division (persons vs. ancestors) changes the outcome.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Dual-Relation Inheritance with Three Female Heirs
Intra-Hanafi dispute on dual-relation inheritance with three female heirs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate inheritance shares for three female heirs where one has dual relationships, using both Abu Yusuf's and Muhammad's methods, and identify the difference in distribution.

Core Idea
When all three heirs are female, Abu Yusuf divides equally into thirds; Muhammad uses ancestor-based shares then adjusts by persons.

We now turn to a more complex scenario involving three female heirs: two with single relationships from different lines, and one with dual relationships. This case demonstrates that the intra-Hanafi dispute extends beyond two-heir situations. Understanding how to apply the two methods consistently to a larger set of heirs is a valuable skill in faraid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three heirs
Heir A: single relationship from female line (e.g., daughter of daughter of daughter). Heir B: single relationship from male line (e.g., daughter of son of daughter). Heir C: dual relationships (e.g., daughter of daughter of son and daughter of son of daughter). All are female.
2
Apply Abu Yusuf's method
Since all are female persons, the estate is divided equally into three shares: each heir receives 1/3.
No distinction is made for dual relationship because persons are identical.
3
Apply Muhammad's method: ancestor-based shares
Assign shares by ancestors: Heir A (single, female ancestor) gets 1 share. Heir B (single, male ancestor) gets 2 shares. Heir C (dual) gets 3 shares (2 from male ancestor, 1 from female ancestor). Total = 6 shares.
These are initial notional shares, not the final distribution.
4
Pool and re-divide by persons if needed
Since all heirs are female, after ancestor-based shares, there is no need to treat anyone as male in persons division? The text says 'then the persons are the same, so another division comes by persons.' This likely means that the shares from the female ancestor side are pooled and divided equally? The text is ambiguous. Let's interpret: Heir C's share from female ancestor (1) is pooled with Heir A's share (1) and Heir B's share? But Heir B's share from male ancestor is 2. Perhaps only the shares from female ancestors are pooled. The text: 'الأبدان متفق تجيء قسمة أخرى باعتبار الأبدان' – since their persons are the same (all female), they then divide the estate equally? But the earlier step already gave them shares. Possibly the meaning is that after ancestor-based totals, if the persons are the same, the final division is equal? But that would contradict the ancestor shares. Alternatively, maybe after ancestor shares, the portion from the female ancestors is pooled and divided equally among all three because they are all female. This is complex. For clarity, we note that the text does not provide a full calculation; it merely states that another division by persons occurs. The exact outcome is not specified.
The passage is incomplete; it only says 'another division comes by persons' without details.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Abu Yusuf, each gets 1/3. Under Muhammad, the ancestor-based shares are 1, 2, and 3 (totaling 6), but the final shares after the person-division are not computed here. The key takeaway is that the methods differ and the final shares will not be equal.

Preferred View and General Rules for Distant Relatives
Presents the preferred view (Abu Yusuf) and rules for inheritance of aunts' children and similar relatives.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of proximity and dual relationship to determine inheritance shares among distant relatives such as children of aunts and uncles.

Core Idea
The nearest relative inherits; if equally close, the one with dual relationship takes precedence.

In the previous lesson, we discussed the dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding the treatment of heirs with dual relationships. This passage presents the preferred view of Abu Yusuf, endorsed by later Hanafi authorities. It then lays down the general rules for distant relatives: closeness to the deceased is the primary criterion, and if closeness is equal, the direction and dual relationship decide.

Guided Path
1
Identify the preferred view
The faradiyyun of Transoxiana and al-Qadi al-Imam choose Abu Yusuf's view over Muhammad's. The key difference is that Abu Yusuf treats the dual-relation heir as two persons, while Muhammad divides by ancestors.
2
Apply the preferred view to specific examples
The passage gives numeric examples: when a dual-relation heir is with a son of a daughter, division is in halves considering persons; with a daughter of a daughter of a daughter and a son of a daughter of a daughter, division is into fifths.
These examples illustrate how the share increases for the dual-relation heir.
3
State the general principle for distant relatives
The principle is 'أقربهم إلى الميت أولى' (the nearest takes precedence). If equal closeness but same direction, the one with dual relationship is preferred. If directions differ, the closer in degree wins.
This is the overarching rule for all distant relatives.
4
Apply the principle to specific cases
Examples: daughter of maternal aunt excludes daughter of son of maternal aunt (closer by degree); daughter of paternal aunt excludes daughter of daughter of maternal aunt (closer by degree despite different direction); daughters of paternal uncles get two-thirds, daughter of maternal aunt gets one-third (since paternal uncles are asaba).
These show how degree overrides direction and how dual relationship resolves ties.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

If he leaves a daughter of a maternal aunt and a daughter of a son of a maternal aunt, the inheritance goes to the daughter of the maternal aunt because she is closer by one degree. Similarly, if he leaves a daughter of a paternal aunt and a daughter of a daughter of a maternal aunt, the daughter of the paternal aunt takes precedence, even though they are of different directions, because she is closer by one degree. Commentary
This passage provides the final authoritative ruling on the earlier disputes. The faradiyyun of Transoxiana affirm that the correct view is Abu Yusuf's, i.e., the heir with dual relationship inherits from both sides as if she were two persons. Al-Qadi al-Imam (likely a later Hanafi authority) endorses this. The passage then applies this principle to specific variations: if the dual-relation heir is accompanied by a son of a daughter (a male), the division is in halves under Abu Yusuf (considering the dual-relation as two daughters, making total shares four, with male getting two). If the dual-relation heir is with a daughter of a daughter of a daughter and a son of a daughter of a daughter, division is into fifths. The second part of the passage (from 'وأما الكلام في أولادهم') shifts to general rules for more distant relatives: children of paternal aunts, maternal uncles, etc. The guiding principle is closeness to the deceased: the nearest relative inherits. If equally close and of the same direction, the one with dual relationship takes precedence. If directions differ, the closer in degree prevails. Specific examples illustrate: a daughter of a maternal aunt excludes a daughter of a son of a maternal aunt (closer by degree); a daughter of a paternal aunt excludes a daughter of a daughter of a maternal aunt (closer by degree, despite different directions). When there are multiple daughters of paternal uncles (male line) and a daughter of a maternal aunt (female line), the paternal side gets two-thirds (as asaba) and the maternal side one-third (as prescribed share). For those with dual relationship among these, the same principles of unity and difference apply. The passage ends abruptly with 'من', likely incomplete.

Key Terms
أقربهم إلى الميت أولى (aqrabuhum ila al-mayyit awla): The nearest relative to the deceased takes precedence in inheritance.
جهة (jihah): Direction or lineage line (e.g., paternal or maternal).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school relies on closeness to the deceased as the primary determinant for distant relatives, with dual relationship breaking ties when closeness and direction are equal.

Dividing Inheritance Among Female Descendants with Multiple Lines: Abu Yusuf vs. Muhammad
Intra-Hanafi dispute on inheritance division among female descendants with multiple connections.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply both Abu Yusuf's and Muhammad's methods to calculate shares for female descendants with different paternal lineages and state the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
When female descendants have different paternal lineages, Abu Yusuf divides equally by individuals; Muhammad divides by the number and gender of their fathers.

In Hanafi faraid, the division among female descendants with different connections to the deceased can be disputed. This lesson explores a specific case involving three such heirs and the intra-madhab disagreement between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. Understanding both methods and the preferred ruling is crucial for accurate inheritance calculations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the heirs and their lineages
Identify the three female descendants: (1) a daughter of a daughter's daughter (two female links), (2) a daughter of a daughter's son (male link), (3) a daughter of a son's daughter (two links: one via male, one via female). Note which have single or double connections.
The 'fathers' in Muhammad's method refer to the immediate ancestor through whom the relationship passes, regardless of gender.
2
Apply Abu Yusuf's method (by individuals)
Abu Yusuf divides the estate equally among all female descendants because their 'bodies' (individuals) are identical—all are females. Give each heir one share, resulting in three equal shares.
This method ignores the lineage differences and treats all as equal.
3
Apply Muhammad's method (by fathers)
Muhammad first determines shares based on the number and gender of each heir's father (ancestor). For a heir with one female father, 1 share; with one male father, 2 shares; with two fathers (one male, one female), 3 shares (sum of 1+2). Total shares = 6.
The heir with two connections is favored because she represents two lineages.
4
Compare the results
Under Abu Yusuf, all get 1/3 each. Under Muhammad, the heir with one male father gets 2/6=1/3, the one with two connections gets 3/6=1/2, and the one with one female father gets 1/6. So the double-connected heir gains more.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) is clear: a half vs. a third for the double-connected heir.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and its rationale
The Qadi Imam and the farid scholars of Transoxiana preferred Abu Yusuf's view. The relied-upon position is that the double-connected heir inherits only through both directions simultaneously but still gets only one share (equal division). This simplifies calculations and treats all female bodies equally.
The tarjih is based on practicality and the principle that females of the same gender are alike in 'body'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن ترك ابنة ابنة وهي ابنة ابن ابنة وترك أيضاً ابنة ابنة ابنة وترك أيضاً ابنة ابن ابنة أخرى فعلى قول أبي يوسف يقسم بينهم باعتبار الأبدان على ثلاثة أسهم لأن أبدانهم متفقة فإن كلهن أناث، وأما عند محمد القسمة على الآباء ثم على الأبدان فيقال لابنة ابنة البنت التي لها قرابة واحدة سهم لأن أباها أنثى ولابنة ابن البنت التي لها قرابة واحدة سهمان لأن أباها ذكر ولمن لها قرابتان لها ثلاثة أسهم من جهتين سهم من جهة إن أباها أنثى وسهمان من جهة إن أباها ذكر فيكون المال بينهم على ستة باعتبار الآباء ثم الأبدان متفق تجيء قسمة أخرى باعتبار الأبدان؛ هذه الجملة على هذا الترتيب أوردها شيخ الإسلام في شرحه. وذكر القاضي الإمام قول محمد رحمه الله على نحو ما ذكر شيخ الإسلام. وقال الفرضيون من أهل ما وراء النهر : إنها ترث بالجهتين عند أبي يوسف. قال القاضي الإمام : وهذا هو الصحيح وهو اختيار القاضي الإمام من أنه على قول أبي يوسف المال في المسألة الأولى من هذا الفصل بينهما أثلاثاً ثلث المال للتي لها قرابتان لأنها في معنى شخصين، وعند محمد القسمة على الآباء
If he leaves a daughter of a daughter who is a daughter of a son's daughter, and also leaves a daughter of a daughter of a daughter, and also leaves a daughter of a son's daughter of another [type], then according to Abu Yusuf, division is based on the bodies (individuals) into three shares because their bodies are identical, since all are females. As for Muhammad, the division is based on the fathers, then on the bodies. So it is said: For the daughter of a daughter's daughter who has one connection, one share because her father is female; for the daughter of a son's daughter who has one connection, two shares because her father is male; and for the one who has two connections, three shares: one share from the direction that her father is female and two shares from the direction that her father is male. Thus the estate is divided into six based on the fathers. Then the bodies being the same [but] another division arises based on the bodies. This summary in this order was presented by Shaykh al-Islam in his commentary. The Qadi Imam mentioned Muhammad's statement similarly to what Shaykh al-Islam mentioned. The farid scholars from Transoxiana said: She (the one with two connections) inherits from both directions according to Abu Yusuf. The Qadi Imam said: This is correct, and it is the choice of the Qadi Imam that according to Abu Yusuf's statement, the estate in the first case of this chapter is divided between them in thirds: one third of the estate for the one with two connections because she is like two persons; and according to Muhammad, division is based on the fathers.
Source pages p. 404

Commentary
This passage presents a specific inheritance case and the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. The case involves three female descendants: a daughter of a daughter (whose father is female? actually it's a female line), a daughter of a daughter's son (whose father is male), and a daughter of a son's daughter (with two connections). Abu Yusuf divides the estate equally into three shares because all are females and thus identical in 'body' (i.e., as individuals). Muhammad considers the paternal lineage first: each person gets shares based on the number and gender of their fathers. The one with two connections gets a share from each side. The Qadi Imam prefers Abu Yusuf's view, stating that the woman with two connections inherits from both directions.

Key Terms
ذو قرابتين (dhu qarabatayn): A relative who is connected to the deceased through two different lines (e.g., through both maternal and paternal sides).
جهة (jihah): The direction or line of relationship (e.g., maternal or paternal side).
الآباء (al-aba'): In this context, the 'fathers' refer to the immediate ancestors (male or female) through whom the relationship passes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in this intra-Hanafi dispute, how is the estate divided among the three female descendants?
A) Into six shares based on the number of fathers.
B) Into three equal shares based on the number of individuals.
C) Giving one share to the heir with one female father, two to the one with one male father, and three to the one with two connections.
D) Based on the closeness to the deceased.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi inheritance, for female descendants with different lineages, the operative position is equal division by individuals (Abu Yusuf), not by paternal lineage (Muhammad).

Applying Abu Yusuf's Body Method: Female with Two Connections and a Male Heir
First example of Abu Yusuf's method.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate inheritance shares when a female with two connections and a male descendant (ibn bint) are the sole heirs, following Abu Yusuf's body-based division.

Core Idea
A female with two connections counts as two daughters, giving her share equal to the male's share.

This lesson examines the first example from the passage: a woman who has two connections (e.g., through two different relationships) inherits alongside a son of a daughter (ibn bint). Abu Yusuf's method treats the female as having the share of two daughters, leading to a straightforward division into halves.

Guided Path
1
Identify the heirs
List the heirs: a female with two connections and a male (ibn bint). Nobody is excluded.
Both are dhawi al-arham.
2
Determine the method
Apply Abu Yusuf's method of division by bodies, as chosen by the Qadi Imam.
This differs from Muhammad's method.
3
Apply the equivalence principle
The female with two connections is equivalent to two daughters.
This increases her share proportionally.
4
Apply the male:female ratio
Each male gets double a female. The male counts as 2 shares. The female, as two daughters, gets 1 share per daughter = 2 shares.
Total shares = 2 (male) + 2 (female) = 4.
5
Distribute the estate
Each heir gets their portion: the male gets 2/4 = 1/2, the female gets 2/4 = 1/2.
Thus the estate is divided equally.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن كان مع التي لها قرابتان ابن بنت فعلى قول أبي يوسف رحمه الله تعالى على ما اختاره القاضي الإمام يقسم المال بينهما نصفان يعتبر بالأبدان والتي لها قرابتان بمنزلة ابنتين فيكون المال على أربعة للذكر مثل حظ الأنثيين لكل ذكر سهمان ولكل أنثى سهم، وإن كان مع التي لها قرابتان ابنة ابنة ابنة وابن بنت بنت فعند أبي يوسف القسمة على الأبدان فيكون المال أخماساً للتي لها قرابتان سهمان وللابنة سهمان وللابنة الأخرى سهم على الآباء
If with the one who has two connections there is a son of a daughter (ibn bint), then according to Abu Yusuf's statement based on what the Qadi Imam chose, the estate is divided between them in halves, considering the bodies, and the one with two connections is like two daughters, so the estate is into four: for the male the share of two females, each male gets two shares and each female one share. If with the one who has two connections there is a daughter of a daughter of a daughter (ibnat ibnat ibnah) and a son of a daughter of a daughter (ibn bint bint), then according to Abu Yusuf, division is based on the bodies, so the estate becomes fifths: for the one with two connections two shares, for the daughter two shares, and for the other daughter one share, based on the fathers.

Applying Abu Yusuf's Body Method: Female with Two Connections and Two Female Heirs
Second example of Abu Yusuf's method with multiple female heirs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate inheritance shares when a female with two connections is joined by two female heirs (ibnat ibnat ibnah and ibn bint bint) using Abu Yusuf's body-based division.

Core Idea
When multiple female heirs have different connections, Abu Yusuf counts each connection as a separate body, leading to a fifths division.

This lesson examines the second example from the passage: a woman with two connections inherits alongside a daughter of a daughter's daughter (ibnat ibnat ibnah) and a son of a daughter's daughter (ibn bint bint). The female with two connections gets more shares because of her multiple connections.

Identify the heirs

Determine the method
Apply Abu Yusuf's body-based division.
This is the chosen method.

She is equivalent to two daughters.
She gets 2 shares as two daughters.
4

General Rules for Distant Relatives and the Preference for Children of 'Asabah
Sets out general principles and examples for inheriting among distant relatives through common ancestry.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general rules for inheritance among dhawi al-arham, apply the preference for a child of an 'asbah, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between the zahir al-riwayah and Abu 'Imran's narration.

Core Idea
Among distant relatives, the closest in degree inherits; if equal, the one with two connections is preferred; direction matters but 'asabah strength overrides by mufta bihi.

Inheritance among distant relatives (dhawi al-arham) follows specific rules after Quranic heirs and residuaries. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq lays out the general principles: closeness in degree, preference for those with dual lineage, and the controversial role of 'asabah. You will learn the core rules and the important intra-Hanafi difference regarding the child of an 'asbah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary rule
The first principle: the closest in degree to the deceased inherits. This determines priority among distant relatives.
2
Apply the rule of dual connection
If two relatives are equal in degree and their lineages come from the same direction (e.g., both from father's side), the one who is connected through both parents (dhu qarabatayn) is preferred.
3
Examine the dispute over 'asabah
Understand the two narrations within the Hanafi school: according to Abu 'Imran from Abu Yusuf, if directions differ, no preference is given; according to the zahir al-riwayah, the child of an 'asbah is always preferred.
This dispute affects the distribution when a child of an 'asbah and a child of a fixed-share holder are from different directions.
4
Work through examples
Follow the provided examples to see how these rules apply in concrete cases: e.g., combination of daughters of aunts and uncles, and the division between two groups from different sides.
Pay attention to how the rule of 'asabah preference changes the outcome in the two narrations.
5
Note the differences between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad
When there are multiple relatives of equal degree and direction, Abu Yusuf (in one view) divides by number of individuals (by bodies), while Muhammad divides by the number of ancestors. This affects shares in cases like a son and daughter of a maternal uncle.
The passage illustrates this with the example of a son and daughter of a maternal uncle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الكلام في أولادهم وأولاد العمات وأولاد أولاد الأخوال والخالات فنقول : أقربهم إلى الميت أولى فإن استووا في القرب فعند اتحاد الجهة من كان ذو قرابتين يكون أولى، وإن اختلط يقسم المال عليهم على نحو ما ذكرنا بيانه من المسائل. إذا ترك ابنة خالة وابنة ابن خالة فالميراث لابنة الخالة لأتها أقرب بدرجة، وكذلك إذا ترك ابنة عمة وابنة ابنة خالة فإن ابنة العمة أولى وإن كانتا جهتين مختلفتين لأنها أقرب بدرجة وإن ترك بنات العم مع ابنة خالة فلبنات العم الثلثان ولابنة الخالة الثلث وإن كان البعض ذا قرابتين والكلام فيه على نحو ما ذكرنا من اتحاد الجهة واختلافها بيانه فيما إذا ترك ثلاثة بنات عمات متفرقات فالمال كله لابنة العمة لأب وأم، وكذلك إذا ترك ثلاث بنات خالات متفرقات وإن ترك ابنة خالة لأب وأم وابنة عمة لأب وأم فلابنة العم الثلثان ولابنة الحالة الثلث؛ هذا لأن المساواة بينهما يعني به من الاتصال بالميت موجود حقيقة ولكن القرابتان أقوى سبباً فعند اتحاد الجهة يجعل الأقوى في معنى الأقرب، وكذلك ينعدم عند اختلاف السبب والجهة ولأن توريث ذوي الأرحام باعتبار معنى العصوبة وقرابة الأب في ذلك مقدمة على قرابة الأم فجعل قوة السب كزيادة القرب عند اتحاد الجهة وعند اختلاف الجهة يسقط اعتبار هذا المعنى، فإن كان أحدهما ولد عصبة وولد صاحب فرض فعند اتحاد الجهة يقدم العصبة وولد صاحب الفرض، وعند اختلاف الجهة لا يقدم وتعتبر المساواة في الاتصال بالميت وهي رواية أبي عمران عن أبي يوسف. أما في ظاهر الرواية يقدم ولد العصبة على ولد صاحب الفرض حتى أنه إذا ترك لأب وأم أو لأب وابنة عمة فالمال كله لبنت العم وهذا بلا خلاف لأن الجهة هنا اتحدت. ولو ترك ابنة عم وابنة خال وخالة فلابنة العم الثلثان ولابنة الخال والخالة الثلث على رواية أبي يوسف ولا تقدم بنت العم لكونها ولد عصبة لأن الجهة مختلفة هنا. وفي ظاهر الرواية المال كله لابنة العم فيقدم ولد العصبة مع اختلاف الجهة، وهذا لأن ولد العصبة أقرب اتصالاً بوارث الميت فكان أقرب اتصالاً بالميت فإن قيل: فعلى هذا ينبغي أن تكون العمة أحق المال الخالة لأن العمة ولد العصبة وهو أب الأب والخالة بجميع ليست بولد عصبة ولا ولد صاحب فرض فإنهما ولد أب الأم قلنا: الخالة ولد أم الأم وهي صاحبة فرض فمن هذا الوجه تتحقق المساواة بينهما في اتصال الوارث للميت إلا أن اتصال الخالة بوارث وهي أم فتستحق فريضة الأم واتصال العمة بوارث وهو أب فيتحق نصيب الأب، وإن كان قوم هؤلاء من قوم الأم من بنات الأخوال والخالات وقوم من قبل الأم من بنات العمات والأعمام فالمال مقسوم بين الفريقين أثلاثاً، سواء كان من جانب ذو قرابتين أو كان أحد الجانبين ذو قرابتين ومن الجانب الآخر ذو قرابة واحدة. ثم ما من أصاب كل فريق يترجح فيه من كان ذو قرابتين لأب على من قرابته لأم لأن نصيب كل فريق الاستحقاق له بجهة واحدة وكل واحد منهم إذا انفرد استحق جميع ذلك فعند الإجتماع تراعى قوة السبب بينهم في ذلك للقرابة، فإن استووا في القرابة فالقسمة بينهم على الأبدان في قول أبي يوسف الآخر، وفي قوله الأول وهو قول محمد القسمة على أول من يقع الخلاف به من الآباء بيانه فيما إذا ترك ابن خالة وابنة خالة فالمال بينهم للذكر مثل حظ الأنثيين. وهذا بلا خلاف لأن الآباء قد اتفقت وإن ترك ابن عمة وابنة عم فإن لأب وأم أو لأب فهي أولى لأنها ولد عصبة وابن العمة ليس بولد عصبة ولا ولد صاحب فرض، وإن كانت بنت العم لأم فعلى قول أبي يوسف المال بينهما أثلاثاً باعتبار الأبدان الثلثان لابن العمة والثلث لبنت العم وعلى قول محمد الثلثان لبنت العم والثلث لابن العمة لأم، فإذا كان ابن عمة لأب وأم فهو أولى المال لأنه ذو قرابتين بجميع وكذلك إذا كان ابن عمة لأب لأنه أدلاء بقرابة الأب، وفي استحقاق معنى العصوبة يقدم كانت ابنة عم
As for the discussion regarding their children, and the children of paternal aunts (al-ammat), and the children of the children of maternal uncles (al-akhwal) and maternal aunts (al-khalat), we say: The closest among them to the deceased is most entitled. If they are equal in closeness, then when the direction (jihah) is unified, the one who has two connections is preferred. If mixed, the estate is divided among them as we have explained in the cases. If he leaves a daughter of a maternal aunt (ibnat khalah) and a daughter of a son of a maternal aunt, the inheritance is for the daughter of the maternal aunt because she is closer by one degree. Similarly, if he leaves a daughter of a paternal aunt (ibnat ammah) and a daughter of a daughter of a maternal aunt, the daughter of the paternal aunt is more entitled even if they are from different directions because she is closer by one degree. If he leaves daughters of a paternal uncle (banat al-amm) with a daughter of a maternal aunt, the daughters of the paternal uncle get two-thirds and the daughter of the maternal aunt gets one-third. If some have two connections, the discussion is as we mentioned regarding unity and difference of direction. Its explanation: if he leaves three daughters of paternal aunts of different types, the entire estate goes to the daughter of the paternal aunt by father and mother. Similarly, if he leaves three daughters of maternal aunts of different types. If he leaves a daughter of a maternal aunt by father and mother and a daughter of a paternal aunt by father and mother, then the daughter of the paternal uncle (?) gets two-thirds and the daughter of the maternal aunt gets one-third. This is because equality between them in connection to the deceased exists in reality, but the two connections are a stronger cause. So when the direction is unified, the stronger is treated as the closer. Likewise, it is negated when the cause and direction differ. And because the inheritance of dhawi al-arham is based on the meaning of 'asabah (residuary), and the paternal lineage in that is given precedence over the maternal lineage. So the strength of the cause is made like additional closeness when the direction is unified, and when the direction differs, consideration of this meaning falls away. If one of them is a child of an 'asbah (residuary heir) and a child of a holder of a fixed share, then when the direction is unified, the child of the 'asbah and the child of the fixed-share holder are preferred. When the direction differs, no preference is given, and equality in connection to the deceased is considered. This is the narration of Abu 'Imran from Abu Yusuf. In the zahir al-riwayah, the child of an 'asbah is preferred over the child of a fixed-share holder, so much so that if he leaves for a father and mother or for a father and a daughter of a paternal aunt, the entire estate goes to the daughter of the paternal uncle, without dispute because the direction here is unified. If he leaves a daughter of a paternal uncle, a daughter of a maternal uncle, and a daughter of a maternal aunt, then according to Abu Yusuf's narration, the daughter of the paternal uncle gets two-thirds, and the daughter of the maternal uncle and maternal aunt get one-third. She (daughter of paternal uncle) is not preferred because she is a child of an 'asbah since the direction is different here. In the zahir al-riwayah, the entire estate goes to the daughter of the paternal uncle, so the child of an 'asbah is preferred even with different direction. This is because the child of an 'asbah is closer in connection to the inheritor of the deceased, thus closer connection to the deceased. If it is said: according to this, the paternal aunt (al-ammah) should be more entitled to the estate than the maternal aunt (al-khalah) because the paternal aunt is a child of an 'asbah, i.e., the father of the father, and the maternal aunt is altogether not a child of an 'asbah nor a child of a fixed-share holder; they are children of the father of the mother? We say: the maternal aunt is a child of the mother's mother, and she is a fixed-share holder. So from this consideration, equality is realized between them in the connection of the inheritor to the deceased, except that the connection of the maternal aunt is through a female inheritor, i.e., mother, so she deserves the mother's fixed share, and the connection of the paternal aunt is through a male inheritor, i.e., father, so she deserves the father's share. If there is a group from the mother's side such as daughters of maternal uncles and maternal aunts, and another group from the mother's side such as daughters of paternal aunts and paternal uncles, the estate is divided between the two groups in thirds, whether one side has someone with two connections or one side has two connections and the other side has one connection. Then what falls to each team, the one with two connections for the father is preferred over the one whose connection is for the mother, because the entitlement of each team is from one direction, and each one of them, if alone, would be entitled to all of that. So when they gather, strength of cause among them is considered for the relationship. If they are equal in relationship, then division is based on bodies according to the other statement of Abu Yusuf, and according to his first statement, which is also the statement of Muhammad, division is based on the first ancestor who causes the difference. Its explanation: if he leaves a son of a maternal uncle and a daughter of a maternal uncle, the estate is divided between them with the male getting the share of two females. This is without dispute because the ancestors are unified. If he leaves a son of a paternal aunt and a daughter of a paternal uncle, and the daughter is from a paternal uncle by father and mother or by father, she is more entitled because she is a child of an 'asbah, and the son of a paternal aunt is not a child of an 'asbah nor a child of a fixed-share holder. If the daughter of the paternal uncle is by mother, then according to Abu Yusuf, the estate is divided between them in thirds based on bodies: two-thirds for the son of the paternal aunt and one-third for the daughter of the paternal uncle. According to Muhammad, two-thirds for the daughter of the paternal uncle and one-third for the son of the paternal aunt by mother. If the son of the paternal aunt is by father and mother, he is more entitled to the estate because he has two connections fully. Similarly, if he is a son of a paternal aunt by father, because he is connected through the father's lineage. And in entitlement to the meaning of 'asabah, the one who is a daughter of a paternal uncle is preferred.
Source pages p. 404

Commentary
This long passage lays out the general principles for inheritance among distant relatives (dhawi al-arham). The key rule is: the closest in degree to the deceased inherits first. If they are equal in degree, then if they share the same lineage direction (e.g., both from father's side), the one with two connections (to both parents) is preferred. If directions differ, the estate is divided according to the methods explained earlier. Several examples illustrate this: a daughter of a maternal aunt excludes a more distant relative; a daughter of a paternal aunt excludes a daughter of a maternal aunt's daughter because she is closer. When there are multiple relatives of the same type, the one with stronger lineage gets the full share. The passage also discusses the difference between the narration of Abu 'Imran from Abu Yusuf and the zahir al-riwayah (well-known transmission) regarding whether a child of an 'asbah is always preferred over a child of a fixed-share holder, even if directions differ. According to Abu 'Imran, if directions differ, they are equal; according to the zahir al-riwayah, the 'asbah's child is always preferred. The passage then deals with the case of two groups from different sides and how to distribute between them. Finally, it covers specific examples involving sons and daughters of aunts and uncles, showing how Abu Yusuf and Muhammad differ in some cases.

Key Terms
ذو قرابتين (dhu qarabatayn): A relative connected to the deceased through both parents (e.g., a sibling through both mother and father).
ولد عصبة (walad 'asbah): A child of a residuary heir (e.g., a son of a father's brother).
ولد صاحب فرض (walad sahib fard): A child of a fixed-share holder (e.g., a daughter of a mother).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The daughter of the maternal uncle.
B) The daughter of the paternal uncle.
C) They share equally.
D) It goes to the closest in degree.

Key Takeaway
The general rule for distant relatives is closeness in degree, with preference for dual lineage and, per the mufta bihi, the child of an 'asbah always prevails over the child of a fixed-share holder, regardless of direction.

Priority of Children of Asabah vs. Children of Sahib Fard in Dhawu al-Arham
Expansion of an intra-Hanafi dispute on priority among distant relatives

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on priority when connections differ and apply the mufta bihi ruling to a given inheritance scenario.

Core Idea
Child of an asabah is preferred over child of a sahib fard in the well-known view, but a minority treats them equally.

In Hanafi faraid, distant relatives (dhawu al-arham) inherit only when no primary heirs exist. Among them, a dispute arises over the priority between a child of an asabah (e.g., paternal uncle's daughter) and a child of a sahib fard (e.g., maternal aunt). This lesson unpacks the two positions and the reasoning behind the relied-upon ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
Understand that 'child of asabah' refers to a distant relative connected through an agnatic heir, while 'child of sahib fard' is connected through a Quranic share heir.
Example: paternal uncle is an asabah; maternal aunt is a sahib fard.
2
Recognize the role of connection (jihah)
The term 'jihah' refers to the line of connection to the deceased (e.g., through father or mother). When jihah is the same, there is no dispute: the child of asabah takes priority. The dispute arises when jihah differs.
Same jihah means both relatives are connected through the same parent.
3
Distinguish the two positions
Abu Yusuf (via Abu Imran) holds that when jihah differs, the two are equal in priority. The zahir al-riwayah (well-known position) holds that the child of asabah is always preferred, even when jihah differs.
The example given: daughter of paternal uncle (asabah) takes all over daughter of maternal aunt (sahib fard) when both are distant.
4
Apply the mufta bihi ruling
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the zahir al-riwayah: child of asabah is preferred. Use this in fatwa and distribution.
Al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah affirms this.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن كان أحدهما ولد عصبة وولد صاحب فرض فعند اتحاد الجهة يقدم العصبة وولد صاحب الفرض، وعند اختلاف الجهة لا يقدم وتعتبر المساواة في الاتصال بالميت وهي رواية أبي عمران عن أبي يوسف. أما في ظاهر الرواية يقدم ولد العصبة على ولد صاحب الفرض حتى أنه إذا ترك لأب وأم أو لأب وابنة عمة فالمال كله لبنت العم وهذا بلا خلاف لأن الجهة هنا اتحدت.
If one of them is a child of an عصبة and a child of a صاحب فرض, then when the الميت connection is the same, the child of the عصبة and the child of the صاحب فرض are given precedence. When the connection differs, they are not given precedence, and equality in connection to the deceased is considered. This is the narration of Abu Imran from Abu Yusuf. As for the ظاهر الرواية, the child of the عصبة is given precedence over the child of the صاحب فرض, to the extent that if he leaves [a child of] a father and mother, or a father and a daughter of a paternal aunt, the entire wealth goes to the daughter of the paternal uncle, without disagreement, because the connection here is the same.
Source pages p. 405

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the priority of children of عصبة (such as a paternal uncle) over children of صاحب فرض (such as a maternal aunt) when both are distant relatives (dhawu al-arham). The author presents two positions: The first, from a narration of Abu Imran from Abu Yusuf, states that when the connection (جهة) to the deceased differs, they are treated equally in terms of how closely they are connected to the deceased. The second, from ظاهر الرواية (the well-known Hanafi position), states that the child of an عصبة is always given precedence, even if the connection differs, as illustrated by the example of a paternal aunt (child of عصبة) taking all wealth over a maternal aunt. The reasoning is that the child of an عصبة is closer in connection through the heir (the عصبة). Students should note that this dispute only arises when the relatives are not from the same connection; when the connection is the same, there is no disagreement.

Key Terms
عصبة (asabah): A relative who inherits by agnatic relationship, typically through males.
صاحب فرض (sahib fard): A relative entitled to a fixed Quranic share (fard), such as a mother, daughter, sister.
جهة (jihah): The specific line of connection to the deceased (e.g., through father or mother).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The child of the sahib fard
B) The child of the asabah
C) Both equally
D) The closer degree relative

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that among distant relatives, the child of an asabah is always preferred over the child of a sahib fard, even when their connections differ.

The Two Narrations in the Case of a Daughter of a Paternal Uncle with Maternal Relatives
Faraid case with narration-based rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi narrations regarding the inheritance of a daughter of a paternal uncle when joined by a daughter of a maternal uncle and a maternal aunt, and identify which position is mufta bihi.

Core Idea
In dhawu al-arham, the child of an asaba is preferred, but Abu Yusuf's narration gives a share to others if connections differ.

In faraid, distant relatives (dhawu al-arham) inherit when there are no Quranic heirs or asaba. A key case involves a daughter of a paternal uncle (child of an asaba) competing with maternal relatives. This passage presents two narrations within the Hanafi school, one from Abu Yusuf and the other being the relied-upon position (Zahir al-Riwaya). Understanding this case illustrates the principle of preference for the child of an asaba.

Guided Path
1
Identify the heirs
List the three heirs: daughter of paternal uncle (بنت عم), daughter of maternal uncle (بنت خال), and maternal aunt (خالة). Note their connections: بنت عم is child of an asaba (paternal uncle), while the others are from the mother's side.
2
State the two narrations
According to the narration of Abu Yusuf, بنت عم takes 2/3, and بنت خال and خالة share the remaining 1/3. In Zahir al-Riwaya, بنت عم takes the entire inheritance.
Zahir al-Riwaya is the mufta bihi position.
3
Understand the reasoning
Zahir al-Riwaya gives precedence because the child of an asaba is closer in connection to the heir (the deceased's relative) than the children of a صاحب فرض. Even though connections differ (asaba vs farḍ), the asaba connection is stronger.
The text explains: ولد العصبة أقرب اتصالاً بوارث الميت.
4
Apply the mufta bihi
In practice, the Hanafi fatwa follows Zahir al-Riwaya: give all to the daughter of the paternal uncle.
Abu Yusuf's narration is considered a weaker transmission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو ترك ابنة عم وابنة خال وخالة فلابنة العم الثلثان ولابنة الخال والخالة الثلث على رواية أبي يوسف ولا تقدم بنت العم لكونها ولد عصبة لأن الجهة مختلفة هنا. وفي ظاهر الرواية المال كله لابنة العم فيقدم ولد العصبة مع اختلاف الجهة، وهذا لأن ولد العصبة أقرب اتصالاً بوارث الميت فكان أقرب اتصالاً بالميت فإن قيل: فعلى هذا ينبغي أن تكون العمة أحق المال الخالة لأن العمة ولد العصبة وهو أب الأب والخالة بجميع ليست بولد عصبة ولا ولد صاحب فرض فإنهما ولد أب الأم قلنا: الخالة ولد أم الأم وهي صاحبة فرض فمن هذا الوجه تتحقق المساواة بينهما في اتصال الوارث للميت إلا أن اتصال الخالة بوارث وهي أم فتستحق فريضة الأم واتجمال العمة بوارث وهو أب في تحق نصيب الأب، وإن كان قوم هؤلاء من قوم الأم من بنات الأخوال والخالات وقوم من قبل الأم من بنات العمات والأعمام فالمال مقسوم بين الفريقين أثلاثاً، سواء كان من جانب ذو قرابتين أو كان أحد الجانبين ذو قرابتين ومن الجانب الآخر ذو قرابة واحدة. ثم ما من أصاب كل فريق يترجح فيه من كان ذو قرابتين لأب على من قرابته لأم لأن نصيب كل فريق الاستحقاق له بجهة واحدة وكل واحد منهم إذا انفرد استحق جميع ذلك فعند الإجتماع تراعى قوة السبب بينهم في ذلك للقرابة، فإن استووا في القرابة فالقسمة بينهم على الأبدان في قول أبي يوسف الآخر، وفي قوله الأول وهو قول محمد القسمة على أول من يقع الخلاف به من الآباء
And if he leaves a daughter of a paternal uncle, a daughter of a maternal uncle, and a maternal aunt, then according to the narration of Abu Yusuf, the daughter of the paternal uncle gets two-thirds, and the daughter of the maternal uncle and the maternal aunt get one-third. The daughter of the paternal uncle is not given precedence because she is a child of an عصبة, since the connection here is different. In the ظاهر الرواية, the entire wealth goes to the daughter of the paternal uncle, so the child of the عصبة is given precedence even with different connections. This is because the child of the عصبة is closer in connection to the heir of the deceased, hence closer in connection to the deceased. If it is said: accordingly, the paternal aunt should have more right to the wealth than the maternal aunt, because the paternal aunt is a child of an عصبة, i.e., the father's father, and the maternal aunt is not a child of an عصبة nor a child of a صاحب فرض, since both are children of the mother's father. We say: the maternal aunt is a child of the mother's mother, and she is a صاحب فرض; from this aspect, equality between them in the connection of the heir to the deceased is realized, except that the connection of the maternal aunt to the heir is through the mother, so she deserves the mother's share, and the connection of the paternal aunt to the heir is through the father, so she achieves the father's share. And if there are people from the mother's side, such as daughters of maternal uncles and maternal aunts, and people from the father's side, such as daughters of paternal aunts and paternal uncles, the wealth is divided between the two groups into thirds, whether one side has a double connection or one side has a double connection and the other has a single connection. Then, from what each group receives, preference is given to the one who has a double connection through the father over the one whose connection is through the mother, because the entitlement of each group is by one connection, and each one of them, if alone, would be entitled to all of that. So when they gather, the strength of the cause among them is considered for that connection. If they are equal in connection, then division among them is according to bodies in the other view of Abu Yusuf, and in his first view, which is the view of Muhammad, division is according to the first ancestor where the difference occurs.
Source pages p. 405

Commentary
This passage presents a detailed faraid case involving distant relatives (dhawu al-arham): a daughter of a paternal uncle (بنت عم), a daughter of a maternal uncle (بنت خال), and a maternal aunt (خالة). Two narrations are given: According to a narration from Abu Yusuf, the daughter of the paternal uncle takes two-thirds, and the other two share one-third, because their connections differ and she is not given automatic priority. According to ظاهر الرواية, the daughter of the paternal uncle takes everything, because as a child of an عصبة she is always preferred. The passage then addresses an objection: why is a paternal aunt (عمة) preferred over a maternal aunt (خالة) in some contexts? The answer explains that the maternal aunt is connected through the mother (who is a صاحب فرض), so they are equal in connection to the heir, but the maternal aunt gets the mother's share and the paternal aunt gets the father's share. Next, the text discusses a scenario where there are multiple relatives from both the mother's side and the father's side: the wealth is divided into thirds between the two groups. Then, within each group, those with double connection (through both parents) are preferred over those with single connection. Finally, a dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad arises: if two relatives in the same group are equal in connection, Abu Yusuf's later view divides per capita (on bodies), while his earlier view and Muhammad's view divide per stirpes (according to the first ancestor where the lineage diverges).

Key Terms
ذو قرابتين (dhu qarabatayn): A relative connected to the deceased through both parents.
الأبدان (al-abdan): Per capita distribution.
الآباء (al-aba'): Ancestors for per stirpes division.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Two-thirds
B) One-third
C) Half
D) The whole wealth

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi faraid for dhawu al-arham, the mufta bihi is that the child of an asaba takes all, even when joined by maternal relatives.
