Division Among Multiple Dhawi al-Arham: Preferences and Intra-Madhhab Disputes
Extended rules for multiple dhawu al-arham and intra-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules for dividing inheritance among multiple groups of dhawu al-arham, including the preference for those with double connection, and distinguish between Abu Yusuf's and Muhammad's views on per capita vs per stirpes distribution.

Core Idea
When multiple dhawu al-arham from both sides coexist, wealth is divided into thirds, and within each group, stronger connections and double connection prevail.

The faraid of dhawu al-arham becomes more complex when there are multiple relatives from both the father's and mother's sides. The passage provides a rule: the wealth is divided into thirds between the two groups. Then within each group, those with double connection (connected through both parents) are preferred over those with single connection. Finally, if relatives in the same group are equal in connection, there is a dispute: Abu Yusuf's later view divides per capita (according to bodies), while his earlier view and Muhammad's view divide per stirpes (according to the first common ancestor). Understanding this hierarchy is essential for correct distribution.

Guided Path
1
Separate the heirs into two groups
Identify which heirs come from the father's side (e.g., daughters of paternal uncles/aunts) and which from the mother's side (e.g., daughters of maternal uncles/aunts).
2
Divide the wealth into thirds between the groups
One-third goes to the father's side group, one-third to the mother's side group, and one-third is reserved? Actually the text says 'المال مقسوم بين الفريقين أثلاثاً' which means divided into thirds between the two groups. This likely means each group gets one-third, and the remaining third? Or it means the whole is divided into three parts, with two parts going to one group? Need careful reading. The phrase 'أثلاثاً' usually means into three equal parts. But then it says 'سواء كان من جانب ذو قرابتين...' implying a fixed third for each side? Actually, common Hanafi rule: when both sides have dhawu al-arham, the estate is divided into three parts: one part to the father's side, one part to the mother's side, and one part to the mother's side again? This is confusing. Let's check the source: 'فالمال مقسوم بين الفريقين أثلاثاً' - it literally says the wealth is divided between the two groups into thirds. So each group gets one-third? That would total two-thirds, not full. There must be an understood third part. Possibly it means the wealth is divided into three shares, with one share for the father's side, one for the mother's side, and the third for a specific category? Alternatively, it could mean that the two groups share the wealth in the proportion of one-third each, and the remaining third is for something else? The passage doesn't specify a third entity. I suspect it means that the two groups together take the whole, but the division is into thirds, i.e., one group gets 2/3 and the other gets 1/3? But it says 'بين الفريقين أثلاثاً' which is ambiguous. In standard Hanafi faraid, when there are dhawu al-arham from both sides, the father's side gets 2/3 and the mother's side gets 1/3. That is a known rule. I'll adopt that interpretation: the wealth is divided into three parts, with two-thirds going to the father's side and one-third to the mother's side. This matches the earlier case where the child of asaba (father's side) took 2/3. So I'll teach that.
Common rule: father's side gets 2/3, mother's side gets 1/3.
3
Within each group, prefer those with double connection
Among the heirs of the same side, those related through both parents (dhu qarabatayn) are preferred over those with single connection (e.g., only through mother). They get a larger share from that group's portion.
4
If equal in connection, apply the intra-madhhab rule
If two heirs in the same group are equal in connection (e.g., both single connection), then Abu Yusuf's later view divides per capita (by number of individuals). His earlier view and Muhammad's view divide per stirpes (according to the first common ancestor where their lineages diverge). The mufta bihi is the per stirpes method.
The mufta bihi is Muhammad's view.
5
Calculate final shares
Combine the group allocations and the within-group preferences to determine each heir's share.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو ترك ابنة عم وابنة خال وخالة فلابنة العم الثلثان ولابنة الخال والخالة الثلث على رواية أبي يوسف ولا تقدم بنت العم لكونها ولد عصبة لأن الجهة مختلفة هنا. وفي ظاهر الرواية المال كله لابنة العم فيقدم ولد العصبة مع اختلاف الجهة، وهذا لأن ولد العصبة أقرب اتصالاً بوارث الميت فكان أقرب اتصالاً بالميت فإن قيل: فعلى هذا ينبغي أن تكون العمة أحق المال الخالة لأن العمة ولد العصبة وهو أب الأب والخالة بجميع ليست بولد عصبة ولا ولد صاحب فرض فإنهما ولد أب الأم قلنا: الخالة ولد أم الأم وهي صاحبة فرض فمن هذا الوجه تتحقق المساواة بينهما في اتصال الوارث للميت إلا أن اتصال الخالة بوارث وهي أم فتستحق فريضة الأم واتجمال العمة بوارث وهو أب في تحق نصيب الأب، وإن كان قوم هؤلاء من قوم الأم من بنات الأخوال والخالات وقوم من قبل الأم من بنات العمات والأعمام فالمال مقسوم بين الفريقين أثلاثاً، سواء كان من جانب ذو قرابتين أو كان أحد الجانبين ذو قرابتين ومن الجانب الآخر ذو قرابة واحدة. ثم ما من أصاب كل فريق يترجح فيه من كان ذو قرابتين لأب على من قرابته لأم لأن نصيب كل فريق الاستحقاق له بجهة واحدة وكل واحد منهم إذا انفرد استحق جميع ذلك فعند الإجتماع تراعى قوة السبب بينهم في ذلك للقرابة، فإن استووا في القرابة فالقسمة بينهم على الأبدان في قول أبي يوسف الآخر، وفي قوله الأول وهو قول محمد القسمة على أول من يقع الخلاف به من الآباء
And if he leaves a daughter of a paternal uncle, a daughter of a maternal uncle, and a maternal aunt, then according to the narration of Abu Yusuf, the daughter of the paternal uncle gets two-thirds, and the daughter of the maternal uncle and the maternal aunt get one-third. The daughter of the paternal uncle is not given precedence because she is a child of an عصبة, since the connection here is different. In the ظاهر الرواية, the entire wealth goes to the daughter of the paternal uncle, so the child of the عصبة is given precedence even with different connections. This is because the child of the عصبة is closer in connection to the heir of the deceased, hence closer in connection to the deceased. If it is said: accordingly, the paternal aunt should have more right to the wealth than the maternal aunt, because the paternal aunt is a child of an عصبة, i.e., the father's father, and the maternal aunt is not a child of an عصبة nor a child of a صاحب فرض, since both are children of the mother's father. We say: the maternal aunt is a child of the mother's mother, and she is a صاحب فرض; from this aspect, equality between them in the connection of the heir to the deceased is realized, except that the connection of the maternal aunt to the heir is through the mother, so she deserves the mother's share, and the connection of the paternal aunt to the heir is through the father, so she achieves the father's share. And if there are people from the mother's side, such as daughters of maternal uncles and maternal aunts, and people from the father's side, such as daughters of paternal aunts and paternal uncles, the wealth is divided between the two groups into thirds, whether one side has a double connection or one side has a double connection and the other has a single connection. Then, from what each group receives, preference is given to the one who has a double connection through the father over the one whose connection is through the mother, because the entitlement of each group is by one connection, and each one of them, if alone, would be entitled to all of that. So when they gather, the strength of the cause among them is considered for that connection. If they are equal in connection, then division among them is according to bodies in the other view of Abu Yusuf, and in his first view, which is the view of Muhammad, division is according to the first ancestor where the difference occurs.
Source pages p. 405

Commentary
This passage presents a detailed faraid case involving distant relatives (dhawu al-arham): a daughter of a paternal uncle (بنت عم), a daughter of a maternal uncle (بنت خال), and a maternal aunt (خالة). Two narrations are given: According to a narration from Abu Yusuf, the daughter of the paternal uncle takes two-thirds, and the other two share one-third, because their connections differ and she is not given automatic priority. According to ظاهر الرواية, the daughter of the paternal uncle takes everything, because as a child of an عصبة she is always preferred. The passage then addresses an objection: why is a paternal aunt (عمة) preferred over a maternal aunt (خالة) in some contexts? The answer explains that the maternal aunt is connected through the mother (who is a صاحب فرض), so they are equal in connection to the heir, but the maternal aunt gets the mother's share and the paternal aunt gets the father's share. Next, the text discusses a scenario where there are multiple relatives from both the mother's side and the father's side: the wealth is divided into thirds between the two groups. Then, within each group, those with double connection (through both parents) are preferred over those with single connection. Finally, a dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad arises: if two relatives in the same group are equal in connection, Abu Yusuf's later view divides per capita (on bodies), while his earlier view and Muhammad's view divide per stirpes (according to the first ancestor where the lineage diverges).

Key Terms
ذو قرابتين (dhu qarabatayn): A relative connected through both parents.
الأبدان (al-abdan): Per capita distribution.
الآباء (al-aba'): Ancestors for per stirpes division.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Per capita
B) Per stirpes
C) According to the number of children
D) All to the elder

Key Takeaway
When dividing inheritance among multiple dhawu al-arham, first allocate thirds to the two groups, then prefer double connections, and finally apply per stirpes if equal in connection.

Dividing Inheritance Between Distant Relative Groups
Rule for dividing inheritance between two groups of distant relatives

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the inheritance distribution between father-side and mother-side groups of distant relatives (dhawu al-arham) and apply the Hanafi rule for intra-group division considering double vs. single connection and the Abu Yusuf/Muhammad dispute.

Core Idea
Wealth is split by thirds based on parental side, then by strength of connection within each group.

When there are no primary heirs, distant relatives (dhawu al-arham) inherit. The Hanafi school divides them into two groups: those connected through the father and those through the mother. This lesson explains the fundamental third split and the priority given to relatives with a double connection (through both parents) within each group. It also covers the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding how to distribute when connections are equal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two groups
Separate the distant relatives into those from the mother's side (e.g., daughters of maternal uncles/aunts) and those from the father's side (e.g., daughters of paternal uncles/aunts).
These are dhawu al-arham, not primary heirs.
2
Split the total wealth into thirds
The father-side group receives two-thirds, and the mother-side group receives one-third. This split is independent of the number of individuals.
This is regardless of whether any relative has a double connection or not.
3
Within each group, prioritize by strength of connection
Those with a double connection (through both father and mother) take priority over those with a single connection (through mother only). The double-connected share among themselves, excluding the single-connected.
The logic: each group's share is earned by that one connection; when alone, each would take all, so strength matters.
4
If all in the group have equal connection, determine the distribution method
If all connections are equal (all double or all single), there is an intra-Hanafi dispute. Abu Yusuf's later view: divide per capita (by number of individuals). Muhammad's view (and Abu Yusuf's earlier view): divide per stirpes (according to the first common ancestor of division).
This dispute affects the actual shares received by individuals.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن كان قوم هؤلاء من قوم الأم من بنات الأخوال والخالات وقوم من قبل الأم من بنات العمات والأعمام فالمال مقسوم بين الفريقين أثلاثاً، سواء كان من جانب ذو قرابتين أو كان أحد الجانبين ذو قرابتين ومن الجانب الآخر ذو قرابة واحدة. ثم ما من أصاب كل فريق يترجح فيه من كان ذو قرابتين لأب على من قرابته لأم لأن نصيب كل فريق الاستحقاق له بجهة واحدة وكل واحد منهم إذا انفرد استحق جميع ذلك فعند الإجتماع تراعى قوة السبب بينهم في ذلك للقرابة، فإن استووا في القرابة فالقسمة بينهم على الأبدان في قول أبي يوسف الآخر، وفي قوله الأول وهو قول محمد القسمة على أول من يقع الخلاف به من الآباء
And if there are people from the mother's side, such as daughters of maternal uncles and maternal aunts, and people from the father's side, such as daughters of paternal aunts and paternal uncles, the wealth is divided between the two groups into thirds, whether one side has a double connection or one side has a double connection and the other has a single connection. Then, from what each group receives, preference is given to the one who has a double connection through the father over the one whose connection is through the mother, because the entitlement of each group is by one connection, and each one of them, if alone, would be entitled to all of that. So when they gather, the strength of the cause among them is considered for that connection. If they are equal in connection, then division among them is according to bodies in the other view of Abu Yusuf, and in his first view, which is the view of Muhammad, division is according to the first ancestor where the difference occurs.
Source pages p. 405

Commentary
This passage explains the method of distribution when there are two groups of distant relatives: one group from the mother's side (e.g., daughters of maternal uncles and maternal aunts) and another from the father's side (e.g., daughters of paternal aunts and paternal uncles). The rule is that the total wealth is divided into three parts, with two-thirds going to the father-side group and one-third to the mother-side group, regardless of whether some individuals have a double connection (through both parents) or not. Then, within each group, the distribution is further refined: those with a double connection through the father are preferred over those whose connection is only through the mother, because each group's entitlement is by one connection (either father or mother) and when alone, each would take the whole share. So when multiple claim from that share, the strength of the cause (double connection) gives priority. If two relatives within the same group are equal in connection (both single or both double), then there is a dispute: Abu Yusuf's later view divides per capita (according to the number of individuals), while his earlier view (also held by Muhammad) divides per stirpes (according to the first common ancestor from which the lineages diverge). Students should note that this applies specifically to dhawu al-arham (distant relatives) and not to primary heirs.

Key Terms
ذو قرابتين (dhu qarabatayn): A distant relative connected to the deceased through both paternal and maternal lines.
القسمة على الأبدان (al-qismatu 'ala al-abdan): Per capita distribution: dividing the inheritance equally among all eligible individuals.
القسمة على أول من يقع الخلاف به من الآباء (al-qismatu 'ala awwal man yaqa' al-khilaf bihi min al-aba'): Per stirpes distribution: dividing according to the first common ancestor from which the lineages branch out.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When two groups of distant relatives inherit (mother-side and father-side), the total wealth is divided into:
A) Equal halves
B) Two-thirds to father-side, one-third to mother-side
C) According to the number of individuals in each group
D) According to the closeness of each group to the deceased

Key Takeaway
For distant relatives (dhawu al-arham), the Hanafi school first splits the inheritance into thirds by parental side, then within each side prioritizes double-connected relatives, and if all connections are equal, distribution may be per capita or per stirpes depending on the adopted view.

Per Capita vs. Per Stirpes in Distant Relative Inheritance
Intra-Hanafi dispute on division method

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the two Hanafi views on dividing shares among equally connected distant relatives, and apply the preferred method (per stirpes) to a given inheritance scenario.

Core Idea
When distant relatives share equal connection, Muhammad divides by ancestral stems; Abu Yusuf later divides by individuals.

In inheritance law, dividing a share among a group of distant relatives who have the same degree of connection to the deceased poses a classic legal question: should each individual receive an equal fraction, or should the share be split first according to the number of family branches? The Hanafi school has two positions on this matter, attributed to its two great disciples. This lesson unpacks the dispute and clarifies which view is relied upon in fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the heirs and their connection
First, determine that the heirs are distant relatives (dhawu al-arham) and that they are equally connected to the deceased—e.g., all are children of paternal uncles, each uncle being equally related.
Equal connection means the same degree of kinship from the deceased.
2
Recognize the two methods
Learn the two terms: 'al-abdan' (per capita) divides the share equally among individuals; 'al-aba'' (per stirpes) divides it according to the number of ancestral stems from the first point of divergence.
Per stirpes = by the first ancestor where the lineages split.
3
Attribute each method to the scholars
Abu Yusuf's later view adopts per capita (al-abdan). His earlier view and Muhammad al-Shaybani's position adopt per stirpes (al-aba').
The 'other view' (qawl al-akhar) of Abu Yusuf is his later opinion.
4
Apply the mufta bihi method
In practice, the Hanafi school gives preference to Muhammad's view (per stirpes). Use this method when calculating shares for distant relatives with equal connection.
The practical effect: if two cousins come from two different uncles, the share is first divided into two halves (one per uncle) and then distributed within each branch.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن استووا في القرابة فالقسمة بينهم على الأبدان في قول أبي يوسف الآخر، وفي قوله الأول وهو قول محمد القسمة على أول من يقع الخلاف به من الآباء
If they are equal in connection, then division among them is according to bodies in the other view of Abu Yusuf, and in his first view, which is the view of Muhammad, division is according to the first ancestor where the difference occurs.
Source pages p. 405

Commentary
This short passage isolates a specific intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the method of distributing a share of inheritance among a group of distant relatives who have equal connection (e.g., all are connected through the same parent with a single or double connection). Two views are presented: Abu Yusuf's later view (قول أبي يوسف الآخر) divides per capita (على الأبدان), meaning the share is split equally among the individuals regardless of lineage branching. In contrast, Abu Yusuf's earlier view (also adopted by Muhammad al-Shaybani) divides per stirpes (على أول من يقع الخلاف به من الآباء), meaning the share is divided according to the number of ancestral lines from the first point where the lineages diverge. For example, if two cousins are from different uncles, the division would be based on the uncles, not the individuals. Students should note that this dispute affects the actual distribution amounts and is specific to distant relatives (dhawu al-arham). The Hanafi school typically relies on Muhammad's view (per stirpes) as the mufta bihi.

Key Terms
الأبدان (al-abdan): Per capita division—each individual gets an equal share.
الآباء (al-aba'): Per stirpes division—according to the number of ancestral stems.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Abu Yusuf's earlier view (per stirpes)
C) Muhammad al-Shaybani's view (per stirpes)
D) Both Abu Yusuf's later view and Muhammad's view are equally relied upon.

Key Takeaway
For equally connected distant relatives, the Hanafi mufta bihi divides by ancestral stems (per stirpes), not by individuals (per capita).

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Counting Individuals vs. Mediators in Dhawi al-Arham Inheritance
Intra-Hanafi dispute on division method for distant relatives

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the methods of i'tibar al-abdan and i'tibar al-mudla bihi in Hanafi inheritance, and apply each method to calculate shares for children of maternal uncles and aunts.

Core Idea
Counting individuals or counting the mediator flips shares: Abu Yusuf gives males double, Muhammad gives females double.

When the deceased leaves no primary heirs, distant relatives (dhawi al-arham) inherit. But how do we divide among them? The Hanafi school has an internal debate: should we count each individual heir equally (اعتبار الأبدان) or should we consider the intermediary (المدلى به) through whom they claim? This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents the dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani with a concrete example. Understanding this methodological difference is critical for correctly applying inheritance rules in complex cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case and the heirs
Read the opening scenario: the deceased leaves three classes of collateral relatives — daughters of maternal uncles, daughters of maternal aunts, and daughters of paternal aunts. Note that the text then focuses on a specific subtype: a son and daughter of a maternal uncle from both parents.
The general rule is that paternal side takes precedence (two-thirds for daughters of paternal aunts).
2
State the two opinions
Abu Yusuf's 'other' opinion (اعتبار الأبدان) gives the son two-thirds and the daughter one-third. Muhammad's opinion reverses this: son gets one-third, daughter two-thirds.
Both are within Hanafi school; base text (Kanz al-Daqa'iq) likely states only one view.
3
Analyze the underlying principle
Abu Yusuf counts each individual, so male gets double female. Muhammad counts the intermediary (the parent); since the parent is a single entity, the two children split equally but with gender bias? Actually, Muhammad's view yields daughter more — the text does not explain the internal logic, but the key is the method.
The text later shows Abu Yusuf's objection: if the mediator were the sole criterion, division wouldn't change with number of claimants.
4
Examine the objection and response
Abu Yusuf argues that in the case of children of paternal aunts, the mediator (father/mother) is fixed, so shares should be constant despite varying numbers. Muhammad responds that the mediator can legally multiply when there are multiple original kinship relations.
This mirrors a similar dispute in children of daughters (عول).
5
Conclude with practical consequence
In a simple case with one male and one female child of maternal uncle, the two opinions yield opposite shares. In complex cases with multiple claimants, the difference persists. The well-known view from the people of Iraq (Ahl al-Iraq) tends to favor the paternal side overall.
The mufta bihi is not specified here; later Hanafi fatwa manuals may prefer one view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الفرائض
قرابة الأب على قرابة الأم، فإن ترك ثلاث بنات أخوال متفرقات وثلاث بنات خالات متفرقات وثلاث بنات عمات متفرقات فالثلثان لبنات العمات ثم نشرح في ذلك ابن الخالة لأب وأم وابنة الخالة لأب وأم فيكون المال بينهم أثلاثاً في قول أبي يوسف الآخر على اعتبار الأبدان لابن الخالة الثلثان ولابنة الخالة الثلث، وعلى قول محمد رحمه الله على عكس ذلك. فإن كان مع هؤلاء ثلاث بنات أعمام متفرقين فالمال كله لابنة العم لأب وأم خاصة لأن ابنة العم لأب وابنة العم لأم سواء في ذلك أن كل واحدة منهما ليس بولد عصبة ولا ولد صاحب فرض وكلما ترجح ابنة العم لأب وأم على ابنة العمة لأب أو لأم فكذلك يترجح على ابنة العمة لأب فلا يتغير هذا الاستحقاق بكثرة العدد من أحد الجانبين وقلة العدد من الجانب الآخر لأن الاستحقاق المدلى به وهو الأب والأم وذلك لا يختلف بقلة العدد وكثرته وهو سؤال أبي يوسف على محمد في أولاد البنات فإن هناك لو كان المدلى به وهو المعتبر لما اختلفت القسمة بكثرة العدد وقلته كما في هذا الموضع لأن الفرق بينهما لمحمد رحمه الله أن هناك تتعدد الفروع بتعدد المدلى به حكماً وهنا لا يتعدد المدلى به حكماً لأنه إنما يتعدد الشيء حكماً إذا تصور حقيقة ولا يثبت التعدد حكماً بتعدد القرابات . وأما الكلام في أولاد العمات وأولاد الخالات إذا ترك بنت بنت عمة لأب وأم وابن بنت عمة لأب وأم فالمال بينهما للذكر مثل حظ الأنثيين بلا خلاف لأن الأصول قد اتفقت . ترك ابنة عمة لأب وأم وابنة خالة لأب وأم فلابنة العمة الثلثان ولبنت الخالة الثلث. وهذا بلا خلاف، وكذا إذا ترك بنت ابن عمة لأب وأم وابنة ابنة خالة لأب وأم فلبنت ابن العمة الثلثان ولابنة ابن الخالة الثلث. أما الكلام في أعمام الأم وعماتها وأعمام الأب وعماته وأخوال الأم وخالاتها إذا ترك الميت خالة لأم وارثة لها فخالها وخالتها بمنزلة خاله وخالته فإن ترك خالة الأم وعمة الأم فقد ذكر أبو سليمان الجرجاني عن أصحابنا أن المال بينهما أثلاث ثلثاه للعمة وثلثه للخالة وجعلهما على هذه الرواية بمنزلة خالة الميت وعمته. وذكر عيسى بن أبان أن المال كله للعمة وذكر يحيى بن آدم أن المال كله لخالة الأم. وجه رواية أبي سليمان أن في توريث هذا النوع المدلى به قائم مقام الميت فعمة الأم بمنزلة عمة الميت وكذلك خالة الأم بمنزلة خالة الميت وفي عمة الميت وخالته القسمة بينهما أثلاثاً فكذا هذا. وإن الأب وعمة الأب فالمال كله لعم الأب، ولو ترك الأب وعمته وخال الأب وخالته فالمال كله له إذا انفرد أن لأب وأم أو لأب لأنه عصبة وإن كان لأم فالمال بينهما أثلاثاً على الأبدان في قول أبي يوسف الآخر، وعلى المدلى به في قوله الأول وهو قول محمد رحمه الله. وإن كان هناك عمة الأب وخالته فعلى رواية أبي يوسف المال بينهما للذكر مثل حظ الأنثيين كما بينا، وعلى رواية عيسى بن أبان ويحيى بن آدم المال كله لعمة الأب لأنها ولد العصبة وهو ولد أب الأب، ولأنها تدلي بقرابة الأب وقرابة الأب في معنى العصوبة مقدم على قرابة الأم، وإن اجتمع الفريقان يعني عمة الأب وخالة الأب وعمة الأم وخالة الأم لقوم الأب الثلثان ولقوم الأم الثلث ثم قسمة كل جزء بين كل فريق في هذا الفصل كما تقدم. ولا يختلف الجواب بكون أحدهما ذي قرابتين والآخر ذي قرابة واحدة في القسمة عند اختلاف الجهة لكن في نصيب كل فريق يترجح ذو القرابتين والآخر ذو قرابة واحدة على نحو ما بينا في الفصل المتقدم. وإن اجتمع عم الأب وعمته وخالة الأم وخالها فالمشهور من قول أهل العراق أن نصيب الأم وهو الثلث فيقسم بين خالتها وخالها على ثلاثة بفضل الذكر على الأنثى، فإن كانتا من أمه لأن التسوية بين أولاد الأم إذا كانوا يتصلون بالميت وهم أخوة الميت وأخواته، إذا كانوا الأب وأم إذا كانوا يتصلون بوارث الميت فلا تسوية بل يفضل الذكر على الأنثى في رواية الحسن بن زياد وأبي سليمان الجرجاني ونصيب الأب يقسم بين قرابته أثلاثاً وهذا ظاهر. ولو اجتمع ثلاثة أخوال متفرقين أم وعم وعمة أب من أم فعلى الرواية المشهورة من أهل العراق وهم الموروثون من جهتين يقدم من هو لأب. ولو ترك خالتي أم أم لأب فعلى الرواية المشهورة من أهل العراق الثلث لخالتي الأم والثلثان بين العمتين وعمتي ويجعل كأن الأم ماتت وتركت أبوين فللأم الثلث سهم من ثلاثة وللأم الثلثان سهمان من ثلاثة، ثم ما أصاب الأم فهي لمن يدلي بها وأنه لا يستقيم. ولما أصاب الأب ينتقل إلى من المسألة ستة : خال أم الأب وأم عمة أم الأب فعلى الرواية المشهورة عن يدلي به وتصح من أهل العراق فيجعل كأن الأم ماتت عن أبوين ففريضتها من ثلاثة أسهم للأم ينتقل إلى أختها، وسهمان للأب تنتقل إلى أخته فتصير في الحاصل كخالة الأم وللأب عم أم الأب سهم سهمان . وإن ترك ثلاثة أخوال لأب منفردين وثلاث عمات أب متفرقات وثلاث خالات أم متفرقات فعلى القول المشهور من أهل العراق يجعل كأن الأم ماتت وتركت أماً كان المال لها، ثم إنها ماتت عن أبوين فقدر نصيبهما من ثلاثة سهم للأم ينتقل ذلك إلى أختها لأب وأم وسهمان للأم تقسم بين عمة الأب لأب وأم وبين خال الأب لأب وأم على ثلاثة للعمة الثلثان وللخال الثلث وكأن هذا الأب أيضاً مات وترك أبوين وأن هذا للأب وارثاً من جهة أبيه . ومن جهة أمه فنصيب أمه ينتقل إلى العم فانكسر بالأثلاث فيضرب ثلاثة في ثلاثة تصير المسألة، ، وعلى هذا القياس تخرج هذه المسائل والكلام في هؤلاء بمنزلة تسعة فمنه تصح الكلام في آبائهم وأمهاتهم ولكن عند انعدام الأصول، فأما عند وجود أحد الأصول فلا من شيء للأولاد كما لا شيء لأحد من أولاد العمات والخالات عند بقاء عمة أو خالة الميت، ويتصور في هذا الجنس شخص له قرابتان بيانه في امرأة لها أخ لأم وأخت لأب فتزوج أخوها لأمها أختها لابنها وهي أيضاً عمتها لأب وأم وولد لهذا الولد ولد ثم مات الثاني فهذه المرأة خالة ابنة لأبيه وعمة ابنة لأم، ثم الجواب في هذا الفصل على الاختلاف الذي بينا في ذي القرابتين في بنات الإخوة وأولاد الأخوات .
Book of Inheritance. The paternal kinship takes precedence over maternal kinship. If he leaves three daughters of maternal uncles separately, and three daughters of maternal aunts separately, and three daughters of paternal aunts separately, then two-thirds go to the daughters of paternal aunts. Then we explain regarding that: a maternal uncle's son from father and mother and a maternal uncle's daughter from father and mother, so the wealth is divided among them into thirds in the other opinion of Abu Yusuf, based on counting persons: for the maternal uncle's son two-thirds, for the maternal uncle's daughter one-third. And according to Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) it is the opposite. If with these there are three daughters of paternal uncles separately, then all wealth goes specifically to the paternal uncle's daughter from father and mother, because the paternal uncle's daughter from father and the paternal uncle's daughter from mother are equal in that each of them is neither a child of an asaba nor a child of a fixed share holder, and just as the paternal uncle's daughter from father and mother takes precedence over the paternal aunt's daughter from father or mother, so too she takes precedence over the paternal aunt's daughter from father, so this entitlement does not change with the multiplicity of number from one side and scarcity from the other, because entitlement is through the intermediary, which is the father and mother, and that does not vary with scarcity or multiplicity of number. This is Abu Yusuf's objection to Muhammad regarding children of daughters: because there, if the intermediary were the criterion, the division would not differ with multiplicity or scarcity of number, as in this place, because the difference between them for Muhammad is that there the branches multiply through the multiplicity of the intermediary legally, while here the intermediary does not multiply legally, because a thing only multiplies legally if its reality is conceivable, and multiplicity is not established legally through multiplicity of kinship relations. As for the discussion on children of paternal aunts and children of maternal aunts: if he leaves a granddaughter of a paternal aunt from father and mother and a grandson of a paternal aunt from father and mother, the wealth is divided between them with the male receiving the share of two females, without disagreement, because the origins are agreed. If he leaves a daughter of a paternal aunt from father and mother and a daughter of a maternal aunt from father and mother, then for the paternal aunt's daughter two-thirds and for the maternal aunt's daughter one-third. This is without disagreement. Similarly if he leaves a daughter of a paternal uncle's son from father and mother and a daughter of a maternal uncle's daughter from father and mother, then for the paternal uncle's son's daughter two-thirds and for the maternal uncle's daughter's daughter one-third. As for the discussion on maternal uncles and aunts of the mother, paternal uncles and aunts of the father, and maternal uncles and aunts of the mother: if the deceased leaves a maternal aunt from mother who inherits from her, then her maternal uncle and maternal aunt are like his maternal uncle and maternal aunt. If he leaves a maternal aunt of the mother and a paternal aunt of the mother, Abu Sulayman al-Jurjani narrated from our companions that the wealth is divided between them into thirds: two-thirds for the paternal aunt and one-third for the maternal aunt, and he considered them in this narration like the maternal aunt and paternal aunt of the deceased. Isa ibn Aban narrated that all wealth goes to the paternal aunt. Yahya ibn Adam narrated that all wealth goes to the maternal aunt of the mother. The justification of Abu Sulayman's narration is that in this type of inheritance, the intermediary stands in place of the deceased, so the paternal aunt of the mother is like the paternal aunt of the deceased, and similarly the maternal aunt of the mother is like the maternal aunt of the deceased, and with the paternal aunt and maternal aunt of the deceased the division between them is into thirds, so here is similar. If he leaves a father and a paternal aunt of the father, then all wealth goes to the paternal uncle of the father. If he leaves a father, his paternal aunt, a paternal uncle of the father, and his paternal aunt, then all wealth goes to the father alone if he is from father and mother or from father because he is an asaba. If he is from mother, then the wealth is divided between them into thirds based on counting persons in the other opinion of Abu Yusuf, and based on the intermediary in his first opinion which is the opinion of Muhammad. If there is a paternal aunt of the father and a maternal aunt of the father, then according to Abu Yusuf's narration, the wealth is divided between them with the male receiving the share of two females as we explained, while according to the narration of Isa ibn Aban and Yahya ibn Adam, all wealth goes to the paternal aunt of the father because she is a child of an asaba, i.e., child of the father's father, and because she claims through paternal kinship, and paternal kinship is in the sense of asabah, taking precedence over maternal kinship. If the two groups meet, meaning the paternal aunt of the father, the maternal aunt of the father, the paternal aunt of the mother, and the maternal aunt of the mother, then for the father's group two-thirds and for the mother's group one-third. Then the division of each portion among each group in this chapter is as previously mentioned. The answer does not differ whether one has two kinship links and the other has one kinship link in the division when the direction differs, but within the share of each group, the one with two kinship links prevails over the one with a single kinship link in the manner we explained in the previous chapter. If the paternal uncle of the father, his paternal aunt, the maternal aunt of the mother, and her maternal uncle come together, the well-known view of the people of Iraq is that the share of the mother, which is one-third, is divided among her maternal aunt and maternal uncle into three parts with the male having preference over the female, if they are from her mother, because equality among children of the mother when they are connected to the deceased, i.e., the deceased's brothers and sisters, when they are connected to the inheritor of the deceased, there is no equality, rather the male is preferred over the female in the narration of al-Hasan ibn Ziyad and Abu Sulayman al-Jurjani. The share of the father is divided among his relatives into thirds, and this is apparent. If three maternal uncles of different types gather: from mother, from father, and a paternal aunt of the father from mother, then according to the well-known narration from the people of Iraq, those who are inheritors from two directions give precedence to the one from father. If he leaves two maternal aunts of the mother from father, then according to the well-known narration from the people of Iraq, one-third goes to the two maternal aunts of the mother, and two-thirds between the two paternal aunts and my paternal aunt, and it is made as if the mother died leaving parents: for the mother one-third (one share of three) and for the father two-thirds (two shares of three). Then what falls to the mother goes to the one claiming through her, and that is not correct. As for what falls to the father, it transfers to... the case is six: a maternal uncle of the mother's father and a maternal aunt of the mother's father? According to the well-known narration from the people of Iraq, it is made as if the mother died leaving parents: her inheritance is from three shares: one share for the mother transfers to her sister, and two shares for the father transfer to his sister, so the result becomes like a maternal aunt of the mother, and for the father, a paternal uncle of the mother's father has one share? Two shares? If he leaves three separate maternal uncles from father, three separate paternal aunts of father, and three separate maternal aunts of mother, then according to the well-known opinion of the people of Iraq, it is made as if the mother died leaving a mother: the wealth would be hers, then she died leaving parents: the portion of their shares from three: one share for the mother transfers to her sister from father and mother, and two shares for the mother? / father? divided between the father's paternal aunt from father and mother and the father's maternal uncle from father and mother into three: for the paternal aunt two-thirds and for the maternal uncle one-third, and this father also died leaving parents, and that this is for the father as an inheritor from the direction of his father and from the direction of his mother, so the share of his mother transfers to the paternal uncle. Then it is broken by thirds, so multiply three by three: the case becomes... And on this analogy these cases come out, and the discussion regarding these is like nine, from which it becomes correct to discuss their fathers and mothers, but when the original relatives are absent. As for when one of the originals is present, then the children get nothing, just as none of the children of paternal aunts and maternal aunts get anything when a paternal aunt or maternal aunt of the deceased remains. In this category, a person with two kinship links is conceivable. Its explanation: a woman has a brother from mother and a sister from father. Her brother from mother married her sister from his daughter? and she is also her paternal aunt from father and mother. A child was born to this child, then the second died. So this woman is a maternal aunt of the daughter from her father and a paternal aunt of the daughter from her mother. Then the answer in this chapter is based on the difference we mentioned regarding someone with two kinship links in the daughters of brothers and children of sisters.
Source pages p. 406

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses inheritance distribution among distant relatives when the deceased has no direct heirs. The main focus is on the shares of various collateral heirs such as children of paternal aunts, maternal aunts, paternal uncles, etc., and the principles governing their distribution. The text presents multiple opinions from Hanafi scholars, notably the disagreement between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani on whether to distribute based on counting the individuals (اعتبار الأبدان) or based on the intermediary through whom they claim (اعتبار المدلى به). For example, in the case of a maternal uncle's son and daughter from both parents, Abu Yusuf gives the son two-thirds and the daughter one-third, while Muhammad reverses this. The passage also discusses the concept of 'mediator' (مدلى به), which is the person through whom the heir inherits (e.g., the parent). When the origins (اصول) are the same, distribution is straightforward; otherwise, complex calculations may be necessary. Later, the text presents cases involving aunts and uncles of the parents, with multiple narrations from authorities like Abu Sulayman al-Jurjani, Isa ibn Aban, and Yahya ibn Adam, showing disagreement on whether the paternal side or maternal side takes precedence. The well-known opinion from the people of Iraq (أهل العراق) is often cited. The passage ends with a hypothetical scenario of a woman with dual kinship links to illustrate the application of these principles. Overall, this section is a dense elaboration of inheritance rules for distant relatives, highlighting the nuance within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
المدلى به (al-mudlā bihī): The intermediary through whom a distant relative claims inheritance, such as the parent (maternal uncle) in cases of aunts and uncles.
اعتبار الأبدان (iʿtibār al-abdān): The method of dividing inheritance by counting each individual heir, regardless of their intermediary.
اعتبار المدلى به (iʿtibār al-mudlā bihī): The method of dividing inheritance based on the intermediary (parent) through whom the heir claims.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) of the dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding the children of a maternal uncle?
A) The shares between the son and daughter are reversed.
B) The paternal uncle's children inherit nothing.
C) The maternal uncle's children inherit equally regardless of gender.
D) The estate is divided equally among all male heirs.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi inheritance of distant relatives, the method of counting (individuals vs. intermediary) flips the shares between male and female children of the same maternal uncle.

Faraid — Inheritance
beginner
10 min
Basic Rule for Mixed Paternal and Maternal Relatives
First part of the passage establishing the basic division rule.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the basic rule for dividing the estate among mixed paternal and maternal relatives and apply it to simple cases involving aunts and uncles.

Core Idea
Paternal relatives get two-thirds, maternal one-third; within each group, shares follow the standard rules for that line.

In this lesson, we examine the foundational principle for distributing the estate among distant relatives (dhawi al-arham) when both paternal and maternal lines exist. The rule is straightforward: the paternal group receives two-thirds and the maternal group receives one-third. Then each group's share is subdivided according to the rules that would apply if the connecting ancestor were the deceased.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two groups
Separate the relatives into paternal (connected through the father) and maternal (connected through the mother). The father's side includes his aunt, uncle, etc. The mother's side includes her aunt, uncle, etc.
The relative's own gender does not affect group allocation.
2
Allocate shares to groups
The paternal group receives two-thirds of the estate, and the maternal group receives one-third. This is the default division when both groups are present.
This applies only when there are no direct heirs (e.g., children, parents).
3
Divide the paternal share
Within the paternal group, divide the two-thirds among its members according to the rules for siblings of the father: if both male and female, male gets double female; if all same gender, equality. The text says 'أثلاثاً' (by thirds) meaning the shares are calculated assuming the father died and his siblings inherit.
The exact division depends on the specific composition of paternal relatives.
4
Divide the maternal share
Within the maternal group, divide the one-third among its members according to the rules for siblings of the mother: male gets double female. This is based on the mother's hypothetical death and her siblings inheriting.
This rule is the well-known view of the school of Iraq (Hanafi).
5
Apply to simple case
Test the rule: if there is a paternal aunt and a maternal uncle, the paternal aunt gets 2/3 of the estate? No, she gets a share of the paternal portion. The maternal uncle gets a share of the maternal portion. For example, if only a paternal aunt and a maternal uncle exist, the paternal aunt gets 2/3 of the estate as sole paternal relative, and the maternal uncle gets 1/3 as sole maternal relative.
If multiple relatives on one side, the division among them uses standard sibling inheritance rules.

Source pages p. 407

Commentary
This passage is a series of detailed examples illustrating the distribution of inheritance when paternal and maternal relatives (dhawi al-arham) meet after the immediate heirs are absent. The author is explaining the practical application of the rule that paternal relatives receive two-thirds and maternal relatives receive one-third of the estate. The examples cover various combinations such as aunts and uncles from both sides, and scenarios where some relatives have dual connections (e.g., a person is both a paternal aunt and maternal aunt). The commentary follows the well-known opinion of the 'people of Iraq' (which often aligns with Abu Hanifa's school) but also mentions a different narration from al-Hasan ibn Ziyad and Abu Sulayman al-Jurjani where siblings from the mother's side are not treated equally if they connect through a non-heir. The passage emphasizes that the principles for dividing the portions among each group are consistent: within the maternal group, the male gets twice the female (like siblings), and within the paternal group, the shares are divided by thirds (since children of siblings are not like children of uncles? Actually, the text says 'ثلاثاً' which may mean 'by three' or 'in thirds'). The calculations involve creating hypothetical scenarios where the intermediate ancestors (mother or father) are considered to have died, then dividing the estate accordingly and transferring shares. The final example illustrates the concept of a person with two connections (e.g., a woman who is both a paternal aunt and maternal aunt to the deceased). This is a complex area of faraid, and the passage serves as a parsing exercise in applying the rules of dhawi al-arham.

Key Terms
قرابة الأم (qarābat al-umm): Relatives connected through the mother, inheriting one-third of the estate in dhawi al-arham.
ذو قرابتين (dhū qarābatayn): A relative related through two lines (e.g., paternal and maternal), which gives a stronger claim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 1/2
B) 1/3
C) 2/3
D) 1/4

Key Takeaway
Estate division between paternal and maternal relatives: 2/3 to paternal, 1/3 to maternal; within each group, male preference applies (2:1) for maternal, and equal division (thirds) for paternal.

Dispute on Equality Among Maternal Relatives and Dual Connection
Dispute and complex examples for dual connection and maternal inheritance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the dispute about male-female equality among maternal relatives and calculate shares when a relative has dual connections.

Core Idea
Among maternal relatives connected through a non-heir, males get double females according to the well-known view, but some early Hanafis hold equality.

This lesson delves into the technicalities of distributing the maternal one-third when there are multiple maternal relatives, and addresses the scenario where a relative is connected through both paternal and maternal lines. The text illustrates these complexities with multiple examples and references a dispute within the Hanafi school regarding the equality of male and female maternal relatives.

Guided Path
1
Understand the dispute on maternal equality
The well-known view (people of Iraq) gives males double females among maternal relatives when they are connected through a non-heir. The alternate view (Hasan ibn Ziyad, Abu Sulayman) holds equality. Note the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference).
This dispute only applies when the connecting ancestor is not an heir (e.g., a woman who is not the deceased's mother).
2
Identify the dual-connection scenario
A relative with dual connection (ذو قرابتين) is related through both paternal and maternal lines. The text says they are preferred in the share of their respective group, but the group allocation (paternal or maternal) depends on the line through which they are more directly related?
The example of the woman who is both a paternal aunt and maternal aunt illustrates this.
3
Work through complex example 1
Consider the case with three maternal uncles from different lines (mother, father's brother, paternal aunt from mother). The text says the one from the father is preferred? Actually it says 'من يقدم من هو لأب' - the one from the father is given precedence. This means that when there are multiple claimants from the same maternal share, the one with stronger connection (via father) is preferred.
The exact calculation requires additional details not fully given.
4
Work through the example with two maternal aunts of the mother
The text describes a scenario: if there are two maternal aunts of the mother (from father's side?), the maternal third is divided among them. The method: assume the mother died with parents, then transfer shares.
This hypothetical method helps determine the distribution.
5
Apply the hypothetical death method
The author repeatedly uses the technique: treat the connecting ancestor as if they died, and then distribute their share according to the rules. This is a standard faraid tool for complex inheritance chains.
For example, to divide the maternal third among maternal relatives, assume the mother died and her siblings inherit from her estate, then those shares become the shares from the original estate.

Preceded over the relatives of the mother. Then the answer in this chapter is according to the difference we mentioned regarding the one with two connections among the children of brothers and children of sisters.

Commentary
This passage is a series of detailed examples illustrating the distribution of inheritance when paternal and maternal relatives (dhawi al-arham) meet after the immediate heirs are absent. The author is explaining the practical application of the rule that paternal relatives receive two-thirds and maternal relatives receive one-third of the estate. The examples cover various combinations such as aunts and uncles from both sides, and scenarios where some relatives have dual connections (e.g., a person is both a paternal aunt and maternal aunt). The commentary follows the well-known opinion of the 'people of Iraq' (which often aligns with Abu Hanifa's school) but also mentions a different narration from al-Hasan ibn Ziyad and Abu Sulayman al-Jurjani where siblings from the mother's side are not treated equally if they connect through a non-heir. The passage emphasizes that the principles for dividing the portions among each group are consistent: within the maternal group, the male gets twice the female (like siblings), and within the paternal group, the shares are divided by thirds (since children of siblings are not like children of uncles? Actually, the text says 'ثلاثاً' which may mean 'by three' or 'in thirds'). The calculations involve creating hypothetical scenarios where the intermediate ancestors (mother or father) are considered to have died, then dividing the estate accordingly and transferring shares. The final example illustrates the concept of a person with two connections (e.g., a woman who is both a paternal aunt and maternal aunt to the deceased). This is a complex area of faraid, and the passage serves as a parsing exercise in applying the rules of dhawi al-arham.

Key Terms
ذو قرابتين (dhū qarābatayn): A relative connected to the deceased through two lines (e.g., both paternal and maternal).
المشهور (al-mashhūr): The well-known and relied-upon opinion in the school.

Within the Hanafi school, the well-known view prefers males over females among maternal relatives connected through non-heirs, but there is a legitimate alternate view of equality.

Preference Rules for Dhawi al-Arham by Degree, Origin, and Lineage
Explains three preference rules for Dhawi al-Arham

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three preference rules for Dhawi al-Arham (distant relatives) and apply them to determine who inherits in a given scenario.

Core Idea
Among distant relatives, nearer in degree is preferred; if equal, one through an heir; if different sides, paternal gets double maternal.

In the Hanafi school, distant relatives (dhawi al-arham) inherit when there are no primary heirs or 'asabah. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the rules for preferring one distant relative over another. Understanding these rules is essential for correctly distributing the estate among non-primary heirs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three preference criteria
Read the passage and extract the three rules: (1) closeness of degree, (2) tracing through an heir (origin), (3) paternal vs maternal side.
The author mentions each rule with the phrase 'قال رحمه الله'.
2
Analyze the analogy to 'asabah for degree
The first rule states that nearer relatives are preferred within each category, just as in 'asabah. Consider how the order of 'asabah (son, then grandson, etc.) maps to this rule.
The text explicitly says 'كما في العصبات'.
3
Understand 'origin' and the heir preference
When equal in degree, the one who traces through an heir (a person who actually inherits) is preferred over one who traces through a non-heir. The reasoning: the heir has stronger kinship, as seen in the precedence of a'yan over 'illat.
The commentator gives the example of bani al-a'yan vs bani al-'illat.
4
Examine the proof for paternal vs maternal ratio
The third rule gives paternal side 2/3 and maternal side 1/3. The proof is the practice of 'Umar and Ibn Mas'ud (companion precedent) and the principle that paternal kinship is stronger.
The text says 'لما روينا من قضية عمر وابن مسعود' and 'لأن قرابة الآباء أقوى'.
5
Apply the rules to a scenario
Given a set of distant relatives, determine which rule applies first (degree, then origin, then lineage side) and who inherits what share.
This step solidifies the hierarchy of rules.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الفرائض اختلاف جهة القرابة للأب ضعف قرابة الأم قال رحمه الله : (والترجيح بقرب الدرجة يعني إرثهم بطريق العصوبة فيقدم الأقرب على الأبعد في كل صنف منهم كما في العصبات. قال رحمه الله : (ثم يكون الأصل وارثاً) أي إذا استويا في الدرجة فمن يدلي بوارث أولى من كل صنف لأن الوارث أقوى قرابة من غير الوارث بدليل تقديمه عليه في استحقاق الإرث فكان من يدلي به أقوى وللقوة تأثير في التقديم ألا ترى أن بني الأعيان يقدمون على بني العلات في العصوبة لهذا المعنى. قال رحمه الله : (وعند اختلاف جهة القرابة للأب ضعف قرابة الأم أي إذا كان بعض ذوي الأرحام من جهة الأب وبعضهم من جهة الأم كان لمن هو من جهة الأب الثلثان ومن هو من جهة الأم الثلث لما روينا من قضية عمر وابن مسعود رضي الله عنهما، ولأن قرابة الآباء أقوى فيكون لهما الثلثان والثلث لقرابة الأم، وهذا لا يتصور في الفروع وإنما يتصور في الأصول والعمات والخالات.
Book of Inheritances: The difference in direction of kinship: for the father's side, double the mother's share. He (the author) said: (Preference is by closeness of degree) meaning their inheritance by way of 'asabah, so the nearer is given precedence over the farther in each category of them, as in the 'asabat. He said: (Then the origin is an heir) meaning when they are equal in degree, then the one who traces through an heir is given precedence over every category, because the heir is stronger in kinship than the non-heir, as evidenced by giving him precedence in entitlement to inheritance, so the one who traces through him is stronger, and strength has an effect in prioritization. Do you not see that the paternal half-brothers (bani al-a'yan) are given precedence over consanguine half-brothers (bani al-'illat) in 'asabah for this reason. He said: (And when the direction of kinship differs, for the father's side is double the mother's share) meaning if some of the distant relatives are from the father's side and some from the mother's side, then those from the father's side get two-thirds and those from the mother's side get one-third, based on the case of 'Umar and Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with them) which we narrated, and because the paternal kinship is stronger, so two-thirds go to them and one-third to the maternal kinship. This is not conceivable in branches but only in roots and paternal aunts and maternal aunts.
Source pages p. 408

Commentary
This passage explains the rules for preferring among ذو الأرحام (distant relatives who are not heirs through fixed shares or 'asabah). The author first states that preference is given by closeness of degree, meaning that the relative who is closer in lineage is prioritized over the more distant one within each category. This is analogous to the rule for 'asabah. Then, if two relatives are equal in degree, the one whose line passes through an heir (i.e., a person who actually inherits) is preferred over the one whose line passes through a non-heir. The reason is that the heir has stronger kinship. The commentator gives the example of a'yan (paternal half-brothers) being preferred over 'illat (consanguine half-brothers) in 'asabah. Finally, when the lineage sides differ, the paternal side inherits twice the share of the maternal side: two-thirds for paternal and one-third for maternal. This is based on the precedent of 'Umar and Ibn Mas'ud. The rule applies only to ancestors and aunts, not to descendants.

Key Terms
عصوبة ('asabah): Residuary heirs who take the remainder after fixed shares, by virtue of male line.
درجة (darajah): Closeness in lineage, measured by number of generations from the deceased.
أصل (asl): The ancestor through whom the distant relative traces kinship to the deceased.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the correct order of preference rules for Dhawi al-Arham?
A) Lineage side, then degree, then origin.
B) Degree, then origin, then lineage side.
C) Origin, then degree, then lineage side.
D) Degree, then lineage side, then origin.

Key Takeaway
When no primary heirs exist, the Hanafi school applies three sequential rules to determine which distant relative inherits: first by closeness of degree, then by tracing through an heir, and finally by giving the paternal side double the maternal side.
